滬飛花業公會　推派代表抵京情願 37

(Nanjing) The Shanghai Flying Flower Industry Association sent Xie Zhongle and Bao Guoliang as representatives to Nanjing to petition. Xie and others arrived in Nanjing on the morning of the 6th. According to them, the Ministry of Finance ordered the Jianghai Customs to prohibit the export of waste wadding, mistakenly prohibiting the export of flying flowers as well. The industry was greatly panicked because waste wadding is commonly known as banana flower wadding, also known as broken wadding, which is taken out from banana cotton and worn-out cotton quilts. Flying flowers are various kinds of flying flower scraps produced by spinning mills, which are a major export of our country with considerable annual sales. After the ban, the industry will inevitably be greatly affected, so a meeting was held to decide to send us to Nanjing to petition the Ministry of Finance and the Ministry of Industry and Commerce, requesting that the export of flying flowers be exempted from the same prohibition. After arriving in Nanjing, we have petitioned the Ministry of Finance, and the result is good. We will then petition the Ministry of Industry and Commerce for relief. (6th Dispatch)

全國稻麥改進所　製就新打麥機 43

(Nanjing) The National Rice and Wheat Improvement Institute, in order to improve the method of threshing wheat by farmers in our country, has specially cooperated with the Agricultural College of Jinling University to trial-produce two types of wheat threshing machines suitable for national conditions. The larger one is powered by an engine, requiring about five horsepower, and is worth more than one hundred yuan. The smaller one is an improved foot-operated type, worth only twenty yuan. According to the institute's recent trial, the larger machine can thresh one dou of wheat per minute, and about sixty shi of wheat per day, using only three cans of kerosene. The wheat grains produced have very few impurities, and the results are excellent. Moreover, in addition to threshing wheat, the machine can also thresh beans, sorghum, and millet, etc. The institute plans to build five or six more units within the year for trial use in Anhui, Henan, Shandong, Shanxi, and Shaanxi provinces next year to facilitate promotion. (6th Central News Agency Dispatch)

稽查郵運貨物辦法 44

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Finance, in view of the fact that unscrupulous merchants have been shipping imported goods that should be inspected by mail, has stipulated measures for inspecting goods shipped by mail to prevent smuggling. It is now learned that the Inspectorate General of Customs and the Directorate General of Posts have reached an agreement on the implementation of these measures. However, in order to avoid complicated procedures, it is proposed to exempt imported sporadic goods shipped by mail with a value of less than 55 customs gold units from the procedures for applying for a shipping permit. The proposal has now been submitted to Minister Kong for review and approval. (6th Central News Agency Dispatch)

(Hankou) Six British stokers of the merchant ship Rousselric, which recently arrived here from Australia, were charged in the British Consulate Court for disobeying the captain's orders and assaulting people on the ship. After a trial this morning, they were sentenced to imprisonment ranging from four weeks to twelve weeks. The prisoners will be escorted to Shanghai by the Marine Corps. According to the captain and chief engineer's testimony in court, the lives of the crew were in danger when the prisoners were on board. The prisoners were all undisciplined Irishmen from the Liverpool area. They were often drunk while on duty and assaulted the chief engineer and the cook, and attempted to throw the chief mate into the sea. Two other sailors were also tried today for the same charges, but were acquitted. (6th Reuters Dispatch)

不干涉西班牙內亂　贊助者已有七國　意提出三點請法說明　俄主邀葡國參加協定 57

(Paris) Regarding the issue of non-interference in the Spanish Civil War, the draft agreement proposed by France to Britain mainly advocates that signatory countries should not engage in transactions of various military equipment, military aircraft, and warships to Spain or Spanish Morocco. As of now, in addition to Portugal, which has not yet responded, Britain, Russia, Germany, Italy, Belgium, the Netherlands, and Czechoslovakia have responded or at least expressed their approval in principle. (6th Havas Dispatch)

(Rome) It was announced here today that Prime Minister Mussolini has responded to the French government on the issue of strict neutrality in Spain, expressing his support in principle. (6th National Dispatch)

(Rome) A communique was issued here this afternoon stating that the Italian government agrees in principle with the French government's policy of non-interference in the Spanish Civil War. However, the Italian authorities are now requesting the French government to answer the following three questions: (1) Whether spiritual solidarity with the conflicting parties, as expressed by popular demonstrations, newspaper propaganda, fundraising, and recruitment of volunteers, constitutes a dangerous interference; (2) Whether the guarantee of non-interference will bind individuals as well as the government; (3) Whether the French government will discuss a control plan to guarantee the implementation of the non-interference agreement. (6th Reuters Dispatch)

(Moscow) On August 5, the French Charge d'Affaires, Mr. Bayart, visited the Soviet Foreign Minister. Under the order of the French Foreign Minister, he informed the Soviet government that the French government is very willing for the Soviet Union to accept the principle of non-interference in Spanish internal affairs and to participate in the non-interference agreement between France, Britain, and Germany. On the same day, Mr. Bayart received a reply from the Soviet government. The Soviet government agreed to the principle of non-interference in Spanish internal affairs and is prepared to participate in the non-interference agreement. The Soviet government also wished: (1) In addition to the countries mentioned by the French government, Portugal should also be invited to participate in this agreement; (2) Actions by certain countries to assist the rebels against the legitimate government of Spain should be stopped immediately. (6th TASS Dispatch)

(Paris) The governments of the Netherlands and Czechoslovakia have recently responded to France's proposal for non-interference in the Spanish Civil War, accepting it in principle. (6th Havas Dispatch)

(Rome) Regarding the French proposal for relevant countries to conclude an agreement on non-interference in the Spanish Civil War, it is reported that the Italian government will also submit a reply soon, expressing its acceptance in principle. Government officials stated that the Spanish situation has become an international issue because the Third International is now engaging in insidious activities around the world, inciting unrest, not only in Spain but also in Greece, Czechoslovakia, Argentina, and other countries. Therefore, the position adopted by the Soviet Union deserves special attention. In general, the Italian reply will divide the policy of non-interference and the policy of neutrality into two because the Spanish incident has now developed into a genuine civil war and is not a simple rebellion. Therefore, the solution should be based on the provisions of international law regarding neutral countries. During the American Civil War, Britain and France recognized both the North and the South as belligerent groups and immediately declared neutrality. There is a precedent. The Spanish situation is the same. All countries should adopt a neutral attitude. (According to the principle of non-interference, countries should not assist the rebels, but they can provide assistance to the legitimate government.) (5th Havas Dispatch)

英政府　關心西國大局　始終守不干涉原則　代理外相銷假視事 58

(London) The international situation is becoming increasingly complex. Therefore, Lord Halifax, the Minister of the Crown who is acting as the British Foreign Secretary, has ended his vacation and returned to London today. In the afternoon, he met with various officials to discuss the temporarily suspended negotiations between Britain and Egypt, as well as the overall situation in Spain and the shocking developments in Greece, where Prime Minister Metaxas has established a dictatorship. Developments on the issue of non-interference in the Spanish Civil War are progressing rapidly and seem to be going smoothly. Those responsible believe that there will be no obstacles from Russia and Portugal. However, everyone is anxiously awaiting the Italian government's response to the French note. However, all parties are currently acting in good faith, so it is expected that a compromise can be reached soon. The French government will inform the British government of the results of its inquiries with other capitals at any time. The British government's response to the French note has been welcomed by all newspapers. It is reported that the note clearly stated that the French government is deeply concerned about the consequences that will be caused by foreign support for any side in the Spanish war. The British government also shares this concern. The British government welcomes the immediate establishment of a compromise to save this danger, and does not oppose the major powers most closely related to this issue jointly declaring that they will first secretly prevent the shipment of arms and ammunition from their territories to Spain before engaging in negotiating a general agreement on this issue. All actions of the British government adhere to the principle of non-interference. Therefore, if other governments are prepared to make this statement, the British government is very willing to join. Italian Planes Aid Western Rebel Army; French Authorities Thoroughly Investigate and Obtain Evidence 60

Two Italian planes, which were forced to land in Woran and Lamoroa in Spanish Morocco last week, were thoroughly investigated by French authorities. It was found that they had taken off before July 20th, belonging to the Italian Air Force. It was also discovered that a total of five planes departed at the same time. Due to the hurried preparations, the traces on the planes could not be completely erased, and the pilots did not have time to conceal their real names. The planes were piloted by civilian pilots and air force personnel. Documents found on one of the deceased revealed his real name. The maps carried by the two planes were all made in Italy. The destination of the planes was Mirira and Xiuta. Two planes have now fallen into the hands of the Spanish rebel army. It is now known that after one plane crashed in Woran, a Spanish plane flew above the Italian plane and dropped a package containing the uniforms of Spanish foreign legionnaires and a note written in Italian, which read, "Put on these uniforms and tell the French authorities that you are stationed in Nador as foreign legionnaires. We will send technicians and two barrels of oil to help you take off again. Do not enter the lion's den." (Reuters dispatch, 5th) Early newspapers reported today that twelve German and Italian planes flew to the ladder of Spain on Monday to supply the rebel army for military use. (National Telegram, 5th)

Analysis of the Spanish Civil War and International Relations: The Struggle Between Democracy and Fascism; Italian and German Interference Causes Panic in Britain and France 61

(Moscow) "Krasnaya Zvezda" commented on the Spanish incident, saying, "On July 23rd, the government forces occupied Xilagadala Ma and Xiaerbasaituo in the southeast, which is a turning point in the position of the Spanish government. Madrid was thus able to connect with the seaport and food supply. The war was mainly participated by workers and militias. In the workers' struggle, the National Confederation of Labor of Anarchist Trade Unions also occupied a very important position. Until the outbreak of the rebellion, they were still slacking off on the United Front of the working class, but after the outbreak of the rebellion, they not only urged workers to participate in the anti-fascist war, but also announced their support for the government. Anarchist trade unionists adhered to the principle of 'not asking about politics.' This may be the first time in Spanish history that they have announced their support for the government. Not only in Madrid, but also in Barcelona, anarchist trade unionists closely cooperated with the Socialist Party and the Communist Party, and also participated in the workers' committee with the latter, cooperating with the government through this committee. Therefore, the rebellion of the warlord Fascist Party has become a huge driving force for the unity of all factions of the proletariat. Young people across the country have rushed to serve the government. Not only Catalonia, but even Baskonia, which has always been a stronghold of royalists and counter-revolutionary priests, is also leaning towards the government. Farmers who stood by in the October 1934 rebellion are now also rising up to participate in the war.

"General Franco of the rebel army, in order to obtain military assistance from Germany and Italy, is willing to give Minoerga Island to Italy and the port of Mahan on the island to Germany, in order to prevent French troops from being transported from Africa to France. Obviously, this action by the Spanish counter-revolutionaries endangers the interests of Britain and France. Franco gave Kota Fortress in northern Morocco to Italy, which is directly opposite the Strait of Gibraltar in Britain. Giving Kota to Italy will make Gibraltar no longer the western gateway to the British Mediterranean. Therefore, if this plan is realized, Britain will lose its control over the Mediterranean and the shortest sea route between Asia and Australia. Of course, the interference of Italy and Germany in Spain will inevitably cause panic in Britain and France. The Spanish civil war is increasingly developing into an international conflict. The outcome of the struggle between Spanish democracy and fascism will largely depend on whether peace or war will prevail in the near future." (Tass dispatch, 5th)

Spanish Envoys Abroad Resign One After Another; Consul in Gibraltar Dismissed 62

(London) Since the revolution in Spain, there have been frequent reports of Spanish envoys abroad resigning or disobeying government orders due to differences in their aspirations. According to a telegram from the capital of Romania, the Spanish ambassador to the country and all the personnel of the embassy and consulates have resigned. Villa Fander, the second secretary of the Spanish embassy here, has also resigned. According to news from Geneva, Sanchez, the Spanish consul general there, and the acting representative and secretary stationed in Xiongcheng (the capital of Switzerland), as well as the consul stationed in Jurick City, have also resigned together. (Havas dispatch, 6th)

Warsaw The first secretary of the Spanish Embassy in Warsaw, who is currently serving as the acting representative, sent a telegram to Madrid today, submitting his resignation and simultaneously sending a telegram to the Spanish rebel government in Burgeaus, stating that he and his colleagues are willing to be dispatched. (Reuters dispatch, 5th)

Madrid The Spanish President today ordered the dismissal of Cano Fa, the consul in Gibraltar, and issued a formal statement to the diplomatic community, saying that the rebel army is now using various fraudulent methods to consolidate their position, but the Spanish government has fulfilled its promise to protect foreigners. (National Telegram, 5th)

Under the Cover of Aircraft, Four Thousand Spanish Rebels Cross the Sea; Preparing to Launch a Large-Scale Attack on Marga; Government Forces Have the Upper Hand in the Northern War 63

Port of Tangier According to a reporter from this newspaper who learned from the headquarters of the rebel army in Spanish Morocco, the second batch of 2,000 rebel soldiers departed by boat last night, intending to cross the Strait of Gibraltar and land at Alchichilas Port. The total number of Moroccan rebels heading to the Spanish mainland, including the previous ones, is as many as 4,000. (Havas dispatch, 6th)

Lisbon A radio club here has recently broadcast a message, saying that yesterday afternoon, 3,000 Spanish rebel soldiers, carrying a large number of military supplies and ammunition, took two sea vessels from Xiuta Port in Spanish Morocco, escorted by six aircraft, crossed the Strait of Gibraltar, and landed at Yarchichia Port in southern Spain. (Havas dispatch, 6th)

Gibraltar This afternoon, two merchant ships full of 2,000 Spanish rebel soldiers crossed the Strait of Gibraltar from Xiuta Port in Spanish Morocco and sailed to Alchichia Port on the north coast, with six aircraft soaring in the sky to escort them. A destroyer "Feilangdieshi" belonging to the Spanish government army came and the aircraft threw bombs at the ship, forcing the ship to speed towards the coast of Aisitubo Na (northeast of the Port of Gibraltar). A shell fired by the ship fell north of the racecourse in this port, which is very close to the refugee shelter. Although there was no loss, more than 700 British refugees in the shelter were frightened. (Havas dispatch, 5th)

Gibraltar Today, when a Spanish government destroyer in the Strait of Gibraltar was engaged in an air and naval war with the rebel army, a cannon shell fired from the ship landed on the racecourse and exploded. Two hundred yards away, there was a camp where 800 British refugees from Spain lived. Fortunately, no one was injured. The destroyer sped out of Marga Port and attacked two steamers carrying 2,000 Moroccan rebels, but the escorting aircraft dropped bombs on the ship, forcing it to sail into Aisitubo Na Port. The rebels finally landed safely at Alchichilas Port. (Reuters dispatch, 6th)

Gibraltar Rebel planes today chased the government's patrol ship "Lebangduo," killing one crew member and injuring seven. The ship immediately fled here, sending one of the injured to the hospital, and then sailed to Malaga. At the same time, the Associated Press learned that three government ships bombing Xiuta were also bombed by five rebel planes, and the three ships responded with anti-aircraft guns. (National Telegram, 5th)

Gibraltar A Reuters reporter here drove to Alchichilas in the Bay of Gibraltar today. According to a Spanish rebel officer there, 3,000 soldiers have now been transferred from Spanish Morocco to the interior of Western Arabia. The troops were divided into two merchant ships and one gunboat, including regular troops, foreign legionnaires, and Moroccan soldiers. The three ships also carried 200 machine guns, thousands of grenades, and many heavy vehicles. The revolutionary army plans to continue to transfer 3,000 soldiers from Xiuta to Alchichilas before the end of the week. Therefore, the total number of the revolutionary army will reach 10,000, and they will launch a large-scale attack on Marga, a very important seaport 65 miles northeast of Gibraltar. The seaport is the capital of the Marga Province, surrounded by mountains, and has a beautiful Moorish castle built in the 13th century called Gibraltar Faro overlooking the entire city. Other important buildings, such as the provincial cathedral with a 280-foot-high spire, the cathedral supervisor's residence, the theater, and the bullring, are all very magnificent. There are several berths in the port that can accommodate hundreds of ships. Ships can enter regardless of the wind direction. The total population of the city is 160,000. (Reuters dispatch, 6th)

War Situation in Various Regions: Recent Rebel Attacks Have Failed 64

Madrid A reporter from this newspaper recently learned about the war situation in various regions as follows: (1) A team of government troops on the northern route, under the command of Captain Bulilo, launched an attack on Gordu Ba Province, has arrived between the Gelangya River and Navasailada, and built fortifications there. (2) The rebel army on the front line of the Somo Mountain Pass north of the capital once attacked Qiasige Village yesterday afternoon, but failed. They attacked again today. After the government troops in the village fought bravely, they finally repelled the rebel army, killing 16 enemies, injuring 30, and capturing many. When the rebel army attacked, they encountered an armored vehicle belonging to the government troops, immediately surrounded it, and planned to break through the armor, hoping to kill the government soldiers in the vehicle. However, the government soldiers in the vehicle refused to be captured and immediately fired out through the small holes next to the vehicle, killing a rebel captain on the spot, as well as the Fascist leader of Qiasige Village, Fu Nieer. When the government reinforcements arrived, they dispersed the rebel army, and all the soldiers in the vehicle were able to escape safely. (3) Although the government troops north of the Leong Mountain Pass have not completely controlled Saint Raphael Village, they have been able to prevent the rebel army from advancing south to attack the Guadarama Mountains. The government troops have also attacked the village of Saisididia twice, and the rear reinforcements have also arrived in the village to strengthen their position. Currently, the rebel army is erecting cannons on the high ground of the Leong Mountain Pass to bombard the government troops' positions, and at the same time sending planes to strafe the government troops' headquarters with machine guns in an attempt to resist stubbornly. The government troops there are now dividing their troops to advance towards the Yamada Mountains. The roads are rugged and the march is quite slow, but their morale is very high, believing that they will definitely win. As for the supply of food to the residents of the capital, it has been handled in accordance with the precedents of the European War. The food that each militiaman can receive per day has also been stipulated as follows: 630 centimeters of bread, 20 centimeters of vegetables, 60 centimeters of fat, 20 centimeters of coffee, 50 centimeters of white sugar, 250 centimeters of meat or pork intestines, 200 centimeters of rice, or 500 centimeters of sweet potatoes (which can be exchanged for 100 centimeters of vegetables), and 2.5 liters of wine. (Havas dispatch, 6th)

Progress of Government Forces on the Aragon Province Front 65

Andai According to the received news, the victory of the Spanish government forces over the rebel army in Sastigo has made the road to Zaragoza unimpeded. Although Sastigo is still in the hands of the rebel army, it is in danger of falling at any time. If the government forces were to occupy the area, it would have a significant impact on the future of the civil war. (Reuters dispatch, 6th)

Barcelona A special dispatch from our reporter: The war situation today, especially on the Aragon Province front, has seen great progress for the government forces. The various news items are recorded as follows:

(1) The rebel army's "Black Team" of 9,500 men recently emerged from the city of Zaragoza and was defeated by the regular army and militias belonging to the government near Quindo Village. Countless military supplies and bullets were seized, and many soldiers of the team were captured.

(2) The government army defeated the fascist party army and the restoration party members in Teidiontuo Village (southeast of Zaragoza City) yesterday.

(3) Colonel Santi Wo, commander of the Catalonia Air Force, reported that the government army on the Aragon Province front surrounded a column of rebel army in Sarnaina City (near Huesca City) yesterday and captured 2,000 people. These people immediately turned against the rebels and joined the government army. The government army has now advanced 15 kilometers towards Zaragoza City.

Except for the Xu Aragon Province, there has been no significant change on other fronts, especially in the area of the Zhua Dalama Mountains north of the capital, where the two armies are still guarding their original positions. As for the Gibushiguya Province in the northwest, the war has been quiet for many days, and it is said that it has now resumed, but neither side has made any progress. It is also said that Navarre Province has entered a state of terror. Wherever the rebel army's power reaches, the residents are in danger of their lives at any time. Especially in Yega City, many members of the People's Front have been brutally executed by shooting. In addition, news came from Burgos City, the seat of the rebel pseudo-government, claiming that Prince Asturias, the third son of the deposed King Alfonso XIII, recently joined the rebel army, but the "National Defense Military Government" refused to recruit him. The prince has returned to France in disappointment. Political figures here criticized this move, saying that it shows that General Mula, the rebel commander on the northern route, is not aiming to carry out a restoration, but to create a personal military dictatorship. (Havas dispatch, 5th)

Madrid Sastigo City, near Zaragoza City, is where the entire city of Zaragoza gets its electricity. Fierce fighting took place there today. Foreign Minister Basiya recently told our reporter in detail about the war situation there, saying that because Sastigo City is important, the rebel army specially dispatched two columns from Zaragoza City to the city, attempting to occupy it. The first column, with a total of 2,700 men, met the government army that departed from Barcelona City midway. As a result of the battle, the government army won, capturing 1,300 rebel soldiers and seizing 20 machine guns and 15 cannons. The second column encountered the government army near Pina City and also retreated after being defeated, with 70 people being captured and 3 cannons and countless ammunition being abandoned. Afterwards, three officers and forty-five soldiers of the rebel army were killed. (Havas dispatch, 6th)

Government Naval Base: Flames Soar into the Sky in Burning 66

Lisbon, Portugal The Katai China Grand Naval Base, on which the Spanish government relies to supply its warships with military supplies and fuel, is now burning. According to a ship arriving here, it saw flames rising and thick smoke billowing outside the port, and heard huge explosions. (Reuters dispatch, 6th)

Rebel Army Uses Cavalry in the Guadarama Mountain Area 67

Madrid The great battle for Madrid is gradually becoming serious, so the bloodshed in Spain today is even more tragic. According to the government's announcement that government troops captured the rebel stronghold of Sangrafaer in the Zhua Dalama area, the army immediately intercepted a wireless telegram from the rebel headquarters in Burgos, ordering the rebel army on the Liang Plateau not to hesitate to sacrifice to capture Zhua Dalama Village in order to open the road to Madrid, and ordering them to quickly capture the Zhaoya Reservoir north of the capital, which Madrid relies on for its water source. Today, the rebel army used cavalry for mountain warfare for the first time, but the terrain was unfavorable, and the cavalry team was driven away by the government army's rifles and machine guns. The rebel army claimed that the former royalists in Panpoluna in northeastern Spain had formed a column of 12,000 men and were heading towards Madrid. It also claimed that they had seized 15 trucks full of soldiers and ammunition in Zaragoza, and annihilated a team of government soldiers in Granada, consisting of 250 militiamen loyal to the government. Three cannons, four machine guns, trucks, and ordinary vehicles were all owned by the revolutionary army. The government side claimed that the government army advancing from Barcelona towards Zaragoza surrounded a column of rebel army in Salinina, 35 miles from the city, and captured 2,000 people. (Reuters dispatch, 6th)

Guadarama Rebel Front When Mr. Picard, a reporter for the Associated Press, arrived in Rafir today, the government army was attacking the city. Mr. Picard was detained by the rebel army for four hours. He was released only when the battle ended. According to Mr. Picard's report, the government army suddenly attacked from both wings, intending to encircle the entire Zhua Dalama area. The government troops were all left-wing youths, wearing blue workers' uniforms. They rushed down from Mount Soma. The rebel side was a formal infantry and artillery army, backed by well-trained fascist soldiers, who swept the government army like mowing grass and were all repelled. However, the government army had planes dropping hundred-pound bombs in the air, so the rebel army also suffered heavy losses. The residents of the city all came out in their pajamas to help the fascist army defend the city, using bedding as sandbags or climbing up chimneys to shoot at the enemy. Although the battle has not been decided, the rebel leader told Mr. Picard that Madrid could be occupied this week. (National Telegram, 5th)

Rebel Army in Oviedo Surrounded 68

Northern Route Rebel Headquarters Colonel Alanda, commander of the rebel army in Oviedo, is now surrounded by government troops. Today, he sent a telegram without money to General Mula and General Franco, the commanders-in-chief of the rebel army, asking for help, saying that if he cannot get help immediately, he will not be able to resist any longer. General Mula replied that a large team of rebel army has attacked the northern route to relieve the siege of Oviedo. General Franco telegraphed an order to stand firm. Judging from the fragmentary news obtained here, the position of the rebel army in Oviedo is very critical, and their food is running out. (National Telegram, 5th)

Madrid The Ministry of Military Affairs announced today that the government army is now attacking Kodubai with aircraft and heavy artillery. The city is in danger of falling at any time. Furthermore, a team of rebel army went to Oviedo to lift the siege there, but it has been dispersed by the government army. At the same time, the vanguard of the government army in Sulia Province has also defeated the rebel army and is now preparing to advance towards Zaragoza. (National Telegram, 5th)

No party other than the government can make any transactions with foreign countries. This also affects the rebel party. Therefore, it is not a problem for the Spanish government to put down the rebellion. (Havas dispatch, 6th)

Barcelona The Catalonia government has today confiscated the factories of the American Ford Motor Company and the General Motors Company. Before this, most of the cars in the two factories had been requisitioned by the government for military use. (National Telegram, 5th)

Royal Marriage Between the Netherlands and Sweden 72

(London) According to the Labor Party's organ newspaper, the Daily People's Voice, Princess Zhu Liana of the Netherlands has become engaged to Prince Quesiers of Sweden, and it will be announced soon. At that time, the Queen of the Netherlands will abdicate so that Princess Zhu Liana can inherit the throne. (Havas dispatch, 6th)

Recent Political Developments in Japan: The Current Cabinet Encounters Reefs; Fate to be Decided Between September and October; The Minsei Party Advocates Formulating a Policy Towards China 73

(Tokyo) Recent political developments in Japan are making the reefs of the Hirota Cabinet more and more obvious. It is generally believed that the decision of its fate will be made between September and October. In the general budget for the next fiscal year, the Ministry of the Navy and the Ministry of the Army requested expenditures of more than 1.5 billion yuan, bringing the total budget to 3 billion yuan. However, the financial authorities estimate that they can only obtain a maximum income of 2.7 billion yuan. Therefore, how to find a way to balance income and expenditure is the biggest problem facing the Hirota Cabinet. Whether its life can be extended depends on this. The military also requested that all the army's demands should be funded by issuing new public bonds, and that all national income and increased tax revenue should be used to improve people's livelihoods. However, the financial authorities believe that, given the current economic situation, it is absolutely impossible to issue public bonds indiscriminately. At most, only 100 million yuan can be issued in the coming fiscal year. This is the main point of disagreement within the cabinet. There are also many disputes among the cabinet members regarding national policies. The Ministry of Communications' national electricity industry state-owned enterprise plan is supported by the military, but the Ministry of Education is strongly opposed to it. Private electricity business owners have attacked it even more fiercely. Minister of Education Ping Sheng Pa Sanlang has publicly stated that the electricity state-owned enterprise plan contains elements of state capitalism and yesterday urged Hirota not to adopt it. However, if this plan is rejected, the ministers involved will inevitably resign, and a great upheaval will be unavoidable. At the same time, the proposal to extend compulsory public education is also attracting a lot of attention. If it cannot be passed, the Minister of Education will probably submit his resignation. In short, the cabinet crisis will be difficult to avoid when the National Policy Discussion Council resumes its meetings. Recently, there have been demands in various quarters in Japan that foreign policy should be determined first, and then defense policy. In addition, the Seiyukai and the Minsei Party have repeatedly stated that the cabinet should carefully decide on its foreign policy first so that it can serve as a compass for defense policy. This proposition is becoming more and more powerful. The statement of the Minsei Party is worth noting. The party firmly believes that the government should carefully examine the actual internal and external situation of China, and formulate a strong and effective policy towards China based on realistic considerations, so as to build the necessary fundamental relationship between the two countries and fulfill the common mission of maintaining peace in the Far East. It also urged the government to strive to implement its policy towards China in accordance with the principle of co-existence and co-prosperity that it has always advocated. The Tokyo Nichinichi Shimbun has always advocated an active policy. Today's editorial also advised the government not to expand its military too hastily, so as not to make Soviet Russia feel uneasy, and advocated that Japan should first determine its foreign policy so as to avoid unnecessary arms competition. This kind of opinion has recently become more and more popular and will probably attract great attention. (Central News Agency dispatch, 6th)

Minister of War Terauchi Strongly Advocates: Achieving Broad National Defense; Would Rather Resign Than Fail 74

(Tokyo) Minister of War Terauchi Juichi feels deeply displeased with Prime Minister Hirota's slow progress in fulfilling his promise of reforming the government. He is determined to use personnel changes as an opportunity to spur the government to vigorously implement reform policies. These include national policies regarding national defense, aviation, raw materials, fuel, steel production, and public health, all of which should be thoroughly implemented to strengthen broad national defense. If Prime Minister Hirota ignores these demands, Terauchi will resign, according to a Hualian telegram dated the 6th.

Anglo-Japanese Compromise Plan: Sir Hoare is One of the Originators - Tokyo Newspaper Reveals News 75

(London) A London correspondent for the Tokyo Asahi Shimbun recently revealed that British First Lord of the Admiralty Sir Samuel Hoare is involved in the Anglo-Japanese compromise plan. Responsible parties in London are discussing this rumor with extreme caution, pointing out that Sir Hoare's current position makes it unlikely that he would actively promote such an initiative. Although British opinion is as described above, some Japanese share the desire to improve Anglo-Japanese relations. However, the British are well aware of the many difficulties ahead, especially the power of Japanese extremists, as exemplified by smuggling in North China and the abuse of British Indian Mr. Hu Xin by "Manchukuo" police authorities. Currently, London is not considering recognizing "Manchukuo," as this matter should be decided by the League of Nations. There has also been no discussion regarding the possibility of Anglo-Russian naval talks to extend the principles of the London Naval Treaty to the Far East. According to various Soviet circles, political relations between the two countries must first be improved before such negotiations can begin, according to a Reuters telegram dated the 6th.

Pacific Aviation: Plans to Extend from the Philippines to the Chinese Coast; Preparing to Negotiate with Chinese Authorities 76

(New York) Reports from Guangzhou claim that Pacific Aviation will extend its service from Manila to Macau on September 1st. American airline officials stated today that this information is incorrect, according to a Guomin telegram dated the 4th.

(Washington) Since opening the Pacific air route, American Airlines now hopes to finalize landing locations with Chinese authorities in early autumn, extending the air route from Manila to the Chinese coast, a distance of approximately 700 miles. Connecting this segment will not only complete the Pacific air route but also link global air routes. American Airlines previously negotiated with the Chinese, British, and Portuguese authorities to select a terminal station for the Pacific air route from Guangzhou, Hong Kong, or Macau. However, due to Japanese interference in China and the unwillingness of the British and Portuguese to grant rights to American businesses, negotiations failed and the matter has been shelved until now. It is recently rumored that China may agree to allow American Airlines to establish an airport on a certain section of the coast, indicating that the previous difficulties may soon be resolved, and global flights are imminent. In the future, mail and packages can circle the globe in sixteen and a half days. If passenger service is implemented, the 60 days, 13 hours, and 28 minutes it took to set the world travel record 35 years ago can now be reduced to one-tenth of that time. The speed of progress is astonishing. The global flight routes are listed below:

New York to Frankfurt, Germany: 3,200 miles, 2 days (German company)

Frankfurt to Amsterdam, Netherlands: 225 miles, half a day (German company)

Amsterdam to Penang: 7,625 miles, 5 days (Dutch company)

Penang to Hong Kong: 1,650 miles, 1 day (British company)

Hong Kong to Manila: 700 miles, 2 days (currently by mail ship)

Manila to New York: 2,190 miles, 6 days (American company) Total: 24,560 miles, 16 and a half days, according to a Guomin telegram dated the 5th.

Fortifications in the Tatar Strait: New Convention Takes Effect; Turkish Government Notifies All Nations of Coastal Facilities and Measures 78

Istanbul, Turkey. Regarding the new convention on the Dardanelles and Bosphorus straits, which was previously signed at the Montreux Convention and subsequently approved by the Turkish Parliament, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs has notified the diplomatic representatives of all countries that this new convention will provisionally come into effect on the 5th of this month. It also stipulates the following facilities and measures along the coasts of the two straits:

(1) Radio stations and navigation beacons will be established at Seddulbahir in the Dardanelles Strait and Büyükliman in the Bosphorus Strait. Warships of all countries passing through the straits in accordance with Articles 10 and 14 of the new convention may communicate with these stations;

(2) Saluting battery emplacements will be established at Kumkale in the Dardanelles Strait and Anadolu Kavağı in the Bosphorus Strait;

(3) Pilot stations will be established at Mehmetçik and Saribayir in the Dardanelles Strait and Büyükliman and Haydarpaşa in the Bosphorus Strait;

(4) Commercial land aircraft of all countries may fly over the straits along the Midye to Enez line. Seaplanes may also fly over the Erikli area when necessary. The government will soon issue a notification to all countries regarding prohibited flight zones;

(5) When foreign warships and auxiliary vessels pass through the straits, the captains of these ships shall notify the stations on both sides of the entrance to the straits of the ship's name by radio, and hoist the flag representing the ship's name on the mast;

(6) Any warships that have suffered damage while passing through the straits shall immediately notify the nature and extent of the damage and repairs by radio, and shall comply with the orders issued by the stations at the entrance to the straits, according to a Havas dispatch dated the 5th.

This is completely different from the situation in Spain. It is also difficult to believe that the Communist Party has great power in Greek politics. Since the accession of George II, the political situation has been unstable, and the King has made many efforts to stabilize the democratic system. Unfortunately, the anti-democratic faction has made a comeback, causing the King's efforts to end in failure." The Morning Post reports, "The people of the United Kingdom all hope that Greece will quickly return to tranquility, because Greece has always been an allied nation of the United Kingdom, and its strategically important position in the Mediterranean is of utmost importance. Therefore, from the British perspective, maintaining the stability of the political situation in Greece is beneficial," according to a Havas dispatch dated the 6th.

Travel Notes of Japan (10) (2) 82

— Reporter of this newspaper, Hu Zhongchi, Hu Yizang

By this time, it was already too late to visit another news kingdom—Osaka Mainichi Shimbun. We didn't go until 3 p.m. the next afternoon.

The Osaka Mainichi Shimbun's building is a seven-story building in a modern retro style. Inside, we were received by Kami Numa Kenkichi, a reporter from the East Asia News Agency, and visited for two hours. The editorial office and block making room are on the second floor, the conference room, guest room, Japanese room, photography workshop, and English Mainichi editorial office are on the third floor, the Osaka Mainichi Charity Association office and braille Mainichi editorial office are on the fourth floor, the sales office, delivery area, and two stereotype printing workshops are downstairs, and the electrical room, machine room, paper storage, bathroom, and public dining room are in the basement. The meteorological observatory and pigeon house are on the roof. The mechanical equipment in the main departments, in our opinion, is largely the same as that of Asahi. Telephoto cameras and vacuum transport machines are all equipped there. There are a total of 23 printing presses, some of the fastest of which can print 180,000 newspapers per hour. Dedicated long-distance telephone lines connect to Tokyo in the east and Fukuoka in the west, which is said to be the first such installation created by Osaka Mainichi.

During the visit, we asked Mr. Kami Numa about everything. From his conversation, we not only understood the organizational system of Osaka Mainichi (note), but also learned the general outline of its past history and the various characteristics it possesses.

The Osaka Mainichi Shimbun is the successor to the "Osaka Daily News," which was founded in the Meiji 9th year (1886). The "Osaka Daily News" was renamed "Constitutional Political Party News" after six years, and then renamed "Osaka Daily News" in the Meiji 21st year (1898). In the Meiji 44th year (1911), it merged with the Tokyo "Mainichi Telegraph" and was renamed "Tokyo Nichi-Nichi Shimbun" as a branch of the "Osaka Mainichi Shimbun." As a result, the Osaka Mainichi became very powerful. It kept pace with the Osaka Asahi at the forefront of the Japanese news business.

In the Taisho 11th year (1922), the Osaka Mainichi Shimbun Company founded two special newspapers, the English Mainichi and Braille News. The English Mainichi is the only English-language daily newspaper run by Japanese people in the country, and the famous scholar Dr. Nitobe Inazo is the editor-in-chief. Braille News is a weekly newspaper dedicated to the blind. The entire copy is 16 pages long. The text is made up of raised dots on thick paper that unfortunate blind people can touch and read. The current editor-in-chief is Nakamura Kyota, a blind scholar who graduated from Cambridge University in England.

The astonishing development of the Mainichi Kingdom in recent years is largely due to the former president, Motoyama Hikoichi. He once said a famous sentence: "The authority of the newspaper is directly proportional to the personality of the reporter."

Osaka Mainichi, like Osaka Asahi, also claims that it starts from the centrism of the imperial family and takes a fair and stable attitude towards any problem. It hired a "highly respected" senior veteran of the Japanese news industry, Tokutomi Soho (real name Inoichiro) as a front for the newspaper. In addition to writing occasional essays and current affairs commentaries for the evening editions of Daimai and Tonichi, this old man also continuously published his life's great work "History of the Japanese Nation" in the morning editions of Daimai and Tonichi. He received particularly favorable treatment in this newspaper. His title was a company guest, and his annual salary was 30,000 yen. Such a title and such a huge salary are rare in the Japanese news industry.

The Osaka Mainichi Shimbun Company has now abolished the title of president. The highest responsible person is Board Chairman and Doctor of Law, Oka Minoru. The chief writer is Takaishi Shingo. The total number of employees in the company, including Tokyo Nichi-Nichi, is more than 3,360, which is more than Asahi (the number of employees in Asahi is 3,300).

The total circulation of Osaka Mainichi and its affiliated Tokyo Nichi-Nichi has exceeded two million. However, compared to the Osaka and Tokyo Asahi, the circulation seems to be a little lower. These two news kingdoms are now using all their strength to compete for supremacy. Recently, Osaka Mainichi opened a grand exposition in Koshien with a capital of one million yen, mainly for the purpose of propaganda. Following this, Osaka Asahi held a Kansai gymnastics competition, also for the same purpose. Osaka Asahi has established magnificent Asahi Halls in major cities to connect the feelings of the reader community, while Osaka Mainichi has Japan's only sound film photography car, collecting news films from various places and renting them to all public institutions for screening, to promote the momentum of "Mainichi" from the sidelines.

Based on superficial observations, we can roughly compare these two kingdoms, Mainichi and Asahi: Asahi seems to be younger than Mainichi, and Mainichi seems to be more mature than Asahi. The youthful spirit and the mature spirit each have their own advantages.

Osaka Mainichi Shimbun

Page 9

Record of the Japanese Combined Fleet Arriving in Xiamen: All 76 Vessels, Gathering the Essence 83

Xiamen Correspondence: The Japanese Navy's Combined Fleet, after a month-long grand exercise in the Pacific mandated territories, returned to Keelung, Taiwan, on July 31st. From August 1st to 5th, they conducted offensive and defensive exercises on the sea surface 3,000 nautical miles south of Keelung and 2,000 nautical miles east of Xiamen. On the 4th, the entire fleet left Keelung and Magong harbors. At 7:00 AM on the 5th, the 7th and 8th Squadrons, the 1st and 2nd Destroyer Squadrons, and the 1st and 2nd Submarine Squadrons, along with temporary Class B cruisers and below, arrived in Xiamen first. The 1st, 3rd, and 5th Squadrons, the 1st, 2nd, and 3rd Aviation Squadrons, and special service units consisting of main battleships and aircraft carriers of 10,000 tons or more, arrived in Xiamen around 11:00 AM that morning. The situation is as follows:

Fleet Composition and Strength: (1) 1st Fleet, battleship Nagato, 35,000 tons, Fusō, 30,000 tons; (2) 3rd Squadron, battleship Haruna, 30,000 tons, Kirishima, 20,000 tons; (3) 5th Squadron, Class A cruiser Myōkō, 10,000 tons, Haguro, 10,000 tons, Nachi, 10,000 tons; (4) 7th Squadron, Class B cruiser Aoba, 7,100 tons, Kinugasa, 7,100 tons, Furutaka, 7,100 tons; (5) 8th Squadron, Sendai, 5,200 tons, Jintsū, 5,200 tons, Nagara, 5,170 tons; (6) 1st Destroyer Flotilla, cruiser Abukuma, 5,170 tons, 21st Destroyer Division, Hatsuharu, Nenohi, Hatsushimo, Wakaba, 22nd Destroyer Division, Satsuki, Minazuki, Fumizuki, Nagatsuki, 30th Destroyer Division, Mutsu, Kisaragi, Yayoi, Uzuki; (7) 2nd Destroyer Flotilla, cruiser Naka, 5,200 tons, 6th Destroyer Division, Ikazuchi, Inazuma, Hibiki, 8th Destroyer Division, Amagiri, Asagiri, 19th Destroyer Division, Uranami, Shikinami, Ayanami, 20th Destroyer Division, Shinonome, Oboro, Fubuki; (8) 1st Submarine Flotilla, submarine tender Jingei, 5,160 tons, 18th Submarine Division, submarines No. 53, 54, 55, etc., 19th Submarine Division, submarines No. 56, 57, 58, etc., 28th Submarine Division, submarines No. 59, 60, 63, etc.; (8) 2nd Submarine Flotilla, submarine tender Kinu, 5,170 tons, 12th Submarine Division, submarines No. 68, 69, 70, etc., 30th Submarine Division, submarines No. 65, 66, 67, etc.; (10) 1st Aviation Squadron, Ryūjō, 7,100 tons, Hōshō, 7,500 tons, both aircraft carriers, attached 5th Destroyer Division, Asakaze, Harukaze, Matsukaze, Hatakaze; (10)(1) 2nd Aviation Squadron, aircraft carrier Kaga, 26,900 tons, attached 29th Destroyer Division, Oite, Hayate; (10)(2) 3rd Aviation Squadron, seaplane carrier Kamoi, 17,000 tons, attached 28th Destroyer Division, two ships, names unknown; (10)(3) Special Service Ships, Mamiya, 15,120 tons, Tsurumi, 14,050 tons, Naruto, 14,050 tons. Together with the 6th Destroyer Squadron that arrived at Gulangyu two days earlier, Kuri, Fuyo, Asagao, Wakatake, Sanae, Yūbari, six destroyers, the entire fleet consists of 76 vessels. After arriving in Xiamen, the 1st Submarine Squadron and 2nd Destroyer Flotilla anchored off Gulangyu. The 2nd Submarine Squadron, 1st Destroyer Flotilla, and 7th and 8th Squadrons anchored between Hulishan Fort, Dianyuwei Fort, and Dadeng Lighthouse. The fleet anchored 10 miles outside the port, between Qingyu and Jinmen.

Main Fleet Officers: (1) Commander-in-Chief of the Combined Fleet and Commander-in-Chief of the 1st Fleet, Admiral Sankichi Takahashi; (2) Commander-in-Chief of the 2nd Fleet, Vice Admiral Viscount Takayoshi Katō; (3) Commander of the 3rd Squadron, Vice Admiral Keitarō Hara; (4) Chief of Staff of the Combined Fleet and Chief of Staff of the 1st Fleet, Rear Admiral Naokuni Nomura. Commanders of the other squadrons are all Rear Admiral rank, not listed.

After the arrival of the Japanese main fleet in Xiamen, at 11:00 AM, the Japanese Navy dispatched the destroyer Wakaba to Xiamen to welcome Mayor Shilin Li, Xiamen Fortress Commander Guogeng Lin, City Government Advisor Hongsheng Chen, Japanese Military Attaché Suga, Japanese Consul Ryōtarō Yamada, important merchants and gentry of Japanese and Taiwanese descent, etc., to the flagship Nagato. Li Shilin immediately represented the provincial government in hosting the fleet, and visited Takahashi together with Lin Guogeng, and also visited Katō on the Myōkō. At 12:00 PM, Takahashi hosted a banquet for Li Lin and the Japanese Consul, etc., on the Nagato. All important generals attended the banquet. During the banquet, Takahashi delivered a speech, stating, "The majority of this Combined Fleet is here for training purposes. Although it is a very short time to anchor in Xiamen, we are honored and delighted to be visited by Mayor Li, representative of Chairman Chen, and Commander Lin and other officials and civilians of your country. In these times of global unrest, ensuring peace in East Asia and promoting the civilization of the Orient is the greatest task of both China and Japan. We must share this great responsibility. To this end, China and Japan must strengthen cooperation, learn from each other's strengths and make up for weaknesses, and fully understand each other. Just as China and Japan cannot, geographically, leave the current state, so too, spiritually, we believe there is a greater need for integration. The peace of the Orient must be maintained by the Oriental peoples themselves, and we have this firm resolve. However, we absolutely do not want to close the economic doors of the Orient to Europe and America, or trample on their vested interests. Not only do we not think that way, but we advocate an open-door policy for the entire world, not just for the Orient.

Furthermore, the navies of both countries will always maintain a special friendly relationship. This unique atmosphere of friendship between the two navies can be transferred to the atmosphere of Fujian Province and extended to the whole of China, so as to improve relations between the two countries. We hope to cooperate with each other and advance our mission endlessly.

Finally, I would like to say a word to the Japanese and Taiwanese residents in Fujian: Our fleet is carrying out the above-mentioned national policy of Japan and is working day and night to support the prosperity of the country. You, in this region, should be the driving force for the co-existence and co-prosperity of Japan and China." After the banquet, Li Lin and others returned to Xiamen. At 2:00 PM, Takahashi, Katō, and others landed, first visiting Japanese Consul Yamada on Gulangyu. At 3:15 PM, they crossed to Xiamen and visited Li Shilin at the Municipal Government. At 4:00 PM, they visited Lin Guogeng at the Fortress Headquarters. Afterwards, they toured the city. At 5:00 PM, the Japanese Consul held a tea party at the consulate, hosting Takahashi and more than 20 other important generals, and invited Li Shilin, Lin Guogeng, and representatives from various organizations, communities, gentry, and merchants, as well as Japanese and Taiwanese gentry and merchants, and foreign consuls, to attend. At 7:00 PM, Li Shilin hosted a banquet for Takahashi and other important military officers at Nanputuo Temple. Takahashi and others returned to their ships after 9:00 PM.

Returning to Port: According to Suga, the Naval Attaché at the Japanese Consulate-General in Fujian, the Combined Fleet exercise is being held for the first time in 20 years. The strength of the Japanese Navy today is incomparable to what it was 20 years ago. Therefore, this exercise can be said to be unprecedented. The Japanese Combined Fleet is formed by drawing forces from various fleets. The essence of the Japanese Navy is almost entirely gathered here. Furthermore, the propaganda materials distributed by the Japanese fleet in Taiwan and Xiamen call the Empire the "Invincible Fleet." Their ambition to dominate the seas is evident. In the implementation phase of the "North Defense, Southward Advancement" policy, the "Surface of the South Seas" and "Behind the South Seas" policies have placed the entire South Seas, Australia, and South China within their purview. Moreover, there has been a month-long grand exercise in the South Seas, and the return journey involves a show of force in the Fujian Sea. It cannot be said that this is meaningless. Although the Japanese side strongly denies that there is any intent, the Japanese-language newspapers here published a statement by a Japanese Navy official on the 3rd, stating, "The movement of the Combined Fleet to the Taiwan area is an opportunity for training. Visiting South China, which has close relations with us, is the mission of the fleet. In addition to security duties, we will engage in friendly exchanges with local officials and civilians, and enable fleet soldiers to personally see and deeply understand the Republic of China. Similarly, we hope that Chinese people will take this opportunity to approach and accurately understand the reality of the Imperial Japanese Navy. Those who engage in malicious propaganda are committing a serious insult to the Japanese Navy." This is a statement to dispel rumors, while 76 ships are scattered like stars inside and outside the port of Xiamen, with warships connected end to end and masts in sight, making one almost suspect that the Egret River has become the Red Cliff. When the fleet was in Taiwan, aircraft carriers and aircraft formations soared. The Japanese-language newspapers here also stated that because Xiamen is considered foreign territory, the aircraft of the aircraft carriers were inconvenient to take off and soar, fully displaying their heroic posture. Their words seem to contain regret, and also seem to contain some meaning. (August 6)

Further Progress in Anti-Smuggling in North China: Li Tonghua Comes North to Investigate the Situation, Inspection Offices to Be Set Up on the Ping-Sui Railway 84

Tianjin Correspondence: Li Tonghua, Deputy Director of the Railway Transportation Anti-Smuggling Inspection Office, arrived in Tianjin from Jinan on the evening of the 3rd to investigate the smuggling situation here. He visited Customs Commissioner Xu Liya and Anti-Smuggling Commissioner Spru the morning of the 4th at 10:00 AM to exchange opinions on the anti-smuggling efforts on the Beijing-Shenyang Railway and the Tianjin-Pukou Railway. Xu Liya and Spru described the current situation of ronin smuggling centered on Tianjin. At noon, they accompanied him to inspect the Jindong Station of the Beijing-Shenyang Railway so that he could practically understand the current situation of smuggled goods being transported from Jidong by train. At 9:00 AM on the 5th, Li and Xu went to the Beijing-Shenyang Railway Bureau to visit Director Chen Juesheng and exchange methods for intercepting goods from Jidong, intending to request the Railway Bureau to assist in order to completely eradicate the problem. In the afternoon, he visited Feng Heming, Director of the Tianjin Office of the Tianjin-Pukou Railway, to discuss anti-smuggling efforts in the northern section of the Tianjin-Pukou Railway in detail. Li stayed in Tianjin for two days and was scheduled to go to Ping on the 6th, first investigating along the Ping-Sui Railway, and then returning south after investigating the Beijing-Hankou Railway. According to Li's inquiries from Jinan to the north along the Tianjin-Pukou Railway, the trend of smuggling on passenger trains on the Tianjin-Pukou Railway has almost completely disappeared. Only ronin continue to secretly transport small batches of goods on freight trains, but the situation south of Dezhou is not as rampant as before. However, smuggled goods landed from Qingdao still occasionally pass through Jinan to the south. Smuggling on passenger and freight trains on the Beijing-Hankou Railway is said to be more stringent than on the Tianjin-Pukou Railway due to the establishment of inspection offices along the line. Smuggled goods have almost ceased to be transported on this route for a month. However, the ronin, due to the mountains of goods piled up in Tianjin and the excessive losses, have no choice but to risk smuggling. Therefore, there has recently been the organization of a death squad, carrying weapons, to transport goods to the hinterland of southern Hebei by car and sailboat. In addition, they load goods in Fengtai and transport them to the northwest along the Ping-Sui Railway. The Inspection Office believes that it is necessary to set up inspection branches in the area north of Dezhou on the Tianjin-Pukou Railway, east of Zhoucun on the Jiaoji Railway, and along the entire Ping-Sui Railway. If anti-smuggling efforts in this area are strict, although there is no immediate solution to smuggling in Jidong, North China can temporarily achieve a slight improvement. The Dezhou Inspection Branch has been established for a long time and will soon exert its powers. The Ping-Sui and Jiaoji Railway Branch Offices will be arranged in the field by Ansier after Li himself completes the investigation and returns to Beijing to consult with the Ministry of Finance. In the future, anti-smuggling efforts on the Jiaoji Railway will focus on Zhoucun, while anti-smuggling efforts on the Ping-Sui Railway will focus on Zhangjiakou and Pingdiquan.

The reason why the General Inspection Office believes that there is no need to set up an inspection branch in Tianjin is that there is a Tianjin Customs here. Therefore, the personnel of the Inspection Office who worked in Tianjin before, including Englishman Archie, have all been ordered to return to Pukou to serve. Although Tianjin Customs is making every effort to implement anti-smuggling work, smuggled goods transported daily from Jidong to Tianjin Station still cannot be directly detained. Although smuggled goods transshipped from Tianjin to the south are not transported via the Tianjin-Pukou Railway, ronin charter civilian ships and long-distance buses to transport them along the Ziya River, Daqing River, North-South Grand Canal, and the Jinji and Jinbao Highways. The time of smuggling is mostly at midnight. Customs officers are afraid of provoking accidents if they forcibly intercept them because many ronin carry weapons. Customs Commissioner Xu Liya recently visited Tianjin Mayor Zhang Zizhong, Security Commander Liu Jialuan, and Liu Yanquan, Director of the Wuhe Water Police Bureau, one after another for this matter, requesting assistance from the military and police agencies to intercept them. Various agencies have agreed that since August 3, armed military and police checkpoints have been set up at key intersections in the suburbs of Tianjin, such as Xiyingmen, to assist Tianjin Customs anti-smuggling personnel in interception. Those who are engaged in this business in the Japanese Concession have suffered excessive losses. More than a dozen smuggling firms that could not support themselves and went bankrupt last week. (5th)

Hurricane and Heavy Rain Cause Disaster in Zhangzhou: River Water Surges 15 Feet, Upstream Counties Also Report Flooding 85

Xiamen Correspondence: This hurricane from the South Pacific struck the Philippines, arriving near Dongsha Island on the 1st of this month. At about 2:00 AM on the morning of the 2nd, it landed between Shantou and Xiamen, accompanied by heavy rain. The wind direction was northeast, moving at 35 kilometers per hour, so the wind force was very strong. It lasted for 24 hours and completely left Xiamen after 2:00 AM on the morning of the 3rd. As a result, all maritime transport and small ferries traveling to and from the inland areas of Zhangzhou and Quanzhou were suspended throughout the 2nd. All highway buses in Zhangzhou and Quanzhou were also suspended. Even the small boats crossing between Xiamen and Gulangyu were forced to stop, and transportation was completely cut off. The Zhangzhou-Xiamen telephone line was also blocked. In Zhangzhou, from the night of the 1st to 5:00 AM on the morning of the 3rd, there was torrential rain, which was extremely violent. Mountain torrents poured down from the upper reaches of the Zhang River and the Jiulong River. At the same time, the wind stirred up the sea tide, which flowed back into the river mouth from the port of Xiamen, so that the river water could not be discharged. The river water rose 15 feet in 48 hours. The fields and gardens along the banks of the Zhang River and the Jiulong River were turned into a swamp. The Zhangsong, Zhangfu, Longzhao, and Zhanglong highways were all submerged and suspended. On the night of the 1st, there was heavy rain. On the morning of the 2nd, the water level in the South River had risen five or six feet. In the afternoon, Honglou Society, Xiyao, Xialiao, and Longyantang along the river in the West Gate were all submerged. Punan, Aopu, Pengzhou, Guokeng, Zhangbin, and other places in the Jiulong River basin were also flooded. The waves were raging. Dameixi, Wuqitang, and Xintang in the southern countryside were all flooded. On the evening of the 2nd, the river water had landed in the southern market of Zhangzhou. By 9:00 AM on the morning of the 3rd, the water depth in Yanglaozhou, Chengguan Road, and Xingmin West Road in the southern market of Zhangzhou reached three or four feet. The water depth in Nanshi Street, Longyanying, Xiuwen West Road, and Shiwei reached the knees. At this point, the water level had risen 15 feet compared to before the wind and rain. On the afternoon of the 3rd, the water continued to rise. The deepest points in Longyanying, Shaositu, Guangnan Road, Dingwei South Road, Xiasha, and Yanglaozhou reached four feet, and the shallowest points were also a foot or so. On the night of the 3rd, the water level stabilized and did not rise any further. On that day, floating corpses floated down from the upper reaches of the South River, coming with the mountain torrents from the upper reaches. Therefore, it is known that Nanjing, Pinghe, Changtai, Hua'an, Longyan, and Yongding will also report flooding. This time, the water force in the West Stream was greater than that in the North Stream, so the impact on the villages along the West Stream was also greater. Fortunately, Zhangzhou is a subtropical region, and the autumn rice matures early and has just been harvested, so although there is a disaster, it is not very serious. When Jinshan and other villages in the first district of Nanjing County were hit by the hurricane, dozens of large trees were knocked down and many houses collapsed. Wu, a villager in Jinshan, was crushed to death by a tree. On the 3rd, land and sea transportation resumed. On the 4th, the Zhangsong and Zhangfu highways were damaged and closed for repairs. They did not resume traffic until the 5th. The water in Zhangzhou and along the river began to recede on the morning of the 4th and had completely receded by the morning of the 5th. (August 6)

Li Bai Actively Prepares for War: Central Army and Guangdong Army Arrive at the Guangxi Border, Merchants and Residents of Wuzhou Evacuate, Traffic Obstructed 86

Guangzhou Correspondence: It is recently heard that Li Bai in Guangxi Province is developing a new situation in Nanning. According to visitors returning from Wuzhou yesterday, Li Bai's attitude is quite firm. He held an oath ceremony for anti-Japanese war officials in Nanning on the 1st of this month. More than 200 Guangxi army division and regiment commanders attended. Li Zongren presided over the meeting. After the meeting, the division and regiment commanders returned to their defenses on the same day to preside over military affairs. Therefore, for a time, Guangxi Province was filled with a wartime atmosphere. The Guangxi armies and militias will be divided into four columns to respond to the war. Each column has two divisions of troops and a number of militias. A commander is appointed. Liao Lei, Commander of the 7th Army, serves as the Commander-in-Chief of the First Route, responsible for guarding the Liuzhou, Qingyuan, and Baise areas. Li Pinxian, Commander of the 8th Army, serves as the Commander-in-Chief of the Second Route, responsible for the defense of Guilin, Liuzhou, Fuchuan, and Hexian. Xia Wei, Commander of the 15th Army, serves as the Commander-in-Chief of the Third Route, guarding Wuzhou, Yulin, and the border adjacent to the southern part of Guangdong. Wei Yunsong serves as the Commander-in-Chief of the Fourth Route, guarding the Baise and Huanglubba areas on the Yunnan border. Li Bai initially planned to concentrate heavy troops in Wuzhou. Later, because Wuzhou had no defensible terrain, he decided to abandon Wuzhou and make Teng County the first line of defense on the eastern route. The Zhou Zhaohuang Division stationed there has withdrawn from Wuzhou to the Jieshou, Pingnan, and Teng County areas. At present, all large and small civilian ships in Wuzhou have been chartered clean. All bamboo rafts and wooden rafts berthed in Wuzhou have also been moved to Jilongzhou on the opposite bank of Wuzhou to block the river surface. Merchants and residents in Wuzhou have now been completely evacuated. Cargo transportation has completely stopped. Strong men from various villages near Wuzhou have returned to their units one after another. The situation is very busy. At present, all ferries from Wuzhou to Guangdong have been suspended. Only the Hong Kong-Wuzhou steamships operate as usual. However, they are crowded with evacuees and there is no room to stand. There have been no battles yet. The rumor that the two armies in Fengchuan have been in contact is completely false. However, the Guangxi government's preparations for war are still meticulous. All wartime highway construction in the province, automobile transportation, telephone pole replacements, registration of helmsmen and drivers, and collection of bamboo, wood, and food in various villages have been properly arranged. In addition, defensive fortifications are being built as quickly as possible. Based on this situation, Li Bai's attitude can be seen. (August 9)

Songjiang: Losses from Consecutive Days of Wind and Rain 87

Since the beginning of this year's Great Heat solar term in summer, there have been consecutive days of showers, interspersed with gales. Although the climate is cooler, the rural fields are in the midst of fertilization, and those that have been flooded will inevitably affect the autumn harvest. Farmers are worried. This morning at about 4:00 AM, a storm and rain came together. Half of the rural sheds were destroyed by the wind. Many peaches and plums in the orchards were blown down. The house next to the east side of the county government hall, which was previously the barracks of the 12th Security Brigade, also collapsed in the heavy rain on the evening of the 3rd, with beams and wood collapsing with a crash. Fortunately, no one was injured. After the heavy rain this morning, the rear beam of the Second Hall sank, and the building was about to collapse. After Secretary Shen and Section Chief Chen surveyed the area, they ordered the servants to temporarily block the road passing through the area, and at the same time hired workers to survey and estimate the cost, and reported to request funds for repairs. Summer-like actions in autumn, with continuous rainy weather, the losses in various parties are quite substantial.

Wuxi: Abolishing Fishing Taxes and Miscellaneous Levies 92

The field tax office of the county government in this county sent personnel to collect fishing taxes from fishermen on the shores of Taihu Lake. A total of more than 500 yuan was collected each year. After retaining 171 yuan for the county, the rest was remitted to the provincial government. Recently, the provincial government found that the amount of this tax was very small, tantamount to extortionate levies, so it instructed the county government to abolish it. After County Chief Long received the order, he issued a public notice yesterday that the fishing tax collected would be abolished from the 25th year onwards. However, old debts from before would still need to be collected. In addition, the County Fishery Association was also notified by the county government to all fishermen to organize and establish it before the end of August.

Gaoyou: Entire Grain Merchants Suspend Business 94

The commerce of this county relies on the grain merchants outside the South Gate as its lifeblood. Since the beginning of summer this year, the wheat harvest has been abundant, and manufacturers from Shanghai, Tianjin, Wuxi, and other places have dispatched specialists with postal orders to set up shops and purchase grain. There are over thirty such firms, each using the grain merchants as agents to purchase grain. The larger ones purchase thirty to forty thousand piculs each day, while even the smaller ones purchase around ten thousand piculs. As a result, the grain merchants have finally begun to see a slight turnaround in their fortunes. However, the head of the Business Tax Bureau, Zang Langxuan, suddenly received an order to impose a nutrition tax starting on August 1st, taxing at a rate of five per mille based on value, which is 1.5 fen per picul. Neighboring counties have not implemented this, and its impact is extremely large. On the first day, all grain merchants specially requested the County Chamber of Commerce to negotiate with Bureau Chief Zang, but to no avail. On the second day, all visiting merchants sought to sell their grain elsewhere, and all firms and companies stopped buying. The entire market suspended business for the day, affecting the livelihoods of thousands of people. All the grain merchants decided to send representatives to the Finance Department to petition, and will not stop until their goal is achieved. On the afternoon of the third day, at 4:00 PM, forty to fifty grain merchant firms and over five hundred porters gathered and went to the Party and government organs to petition. Business has now been suspended for three days, causing extremely large losses.

Nantong: Human-Powered Vehicle Labor Dispute Resolved 95

The rickshaw pullers of Nantong's city and suburban areas went on strike en masse, numbering over a thousand people, due to the harsh penalties imposed by the vehicle tax office, excessive tax rates, and the requirement to pay inspection fees. After mediation by both the Party and government, they accepted the rickshaw pullers' petition, which was submitted to the Construction Department by the county government for review and reduction. Business resumed at 6:00 PM on the fifth day.

Zhu Hongquan, a bill collector for the Yuansheng Rice Shop in Tanghui, Jiaxing, collected payments from Chang'an, Xiashi, and other places on the fourth day. He arrived in Jiaxing on the night train. After Shen Ziqi, the manager of the Jinhongxing Rice Shop in Chang'an, went to the bureau to testify, Zhu confessed that he had embezzled private funds and resorted to this scheme. Hangzhou: Bandits Burn and Loot Kaihua County 97

Kaihua County was captured by bandits on July 8th, who indulged in looting and plunder. Although the province sent teams to increase defense and suppress the bandits, the bandit forces were slightly restrained. However, the bandit atmosphere soon intensified again. On August 3rd, at 8:00 PM, over two thousand bandits, divided into six groups, harassed the major villages of the fifth, sixth, seventh, eighth, ninth, eleventh, fifteenth, sixteenth, and thirtieth du (districts) of Xianhua. They burned down forty to fifty civilian houses, took away over thirty residents, and caused property losses exceeding 30,000 yuan. They began to retreat successively on the morning of the fourth day, returning to their old nest in the Jiulong Mountains. The security team, with its disparity in numbers, shortened its defense line to protect the county town. The bandits are currently occupying the Dashan area of the county's fourth du, threatening to invade Suian, Changshan, and Qu County. The situation is critical. Over four hundred refugees from Kaihua, including Zhang Baoshu, jointly telegraphed Chairman Chiang Kai-shek, requesting the dispatch of a large army to suppress and pacify the bandits. The original telegram is as follows: "To Chairman Chiang Kai-shek in Lushan, Most Urgent: Red bandits are rampaging through Kaihua County and other counties in southern Zhejiang. Fully equipped with firearms, they are scattered throughout the countryside, burning, looting, and occupying the Dalong Mountains to form a county-level Soviet government. They are actively distributing food, managing the baojia system, and training militiamen. It is estimated that the total number of pro-bandit civilians in the county has reached 30,000. One part of the bandits is currently occupying the Taishan area in the eastern countryside, threatening to invade Suian, Changshan, and Quzhou counties, seeking to establish connections. Rumors are rampant. However, the provincial troops are weak and unable to provide rescue. We respectfully telegraph to Your Excellency, requesting the swift dispatch of a large army to suppress and pacify the bandits, to quell the bandit atmosphere. Kaihua will be fortunate, and all of Zhejiang will be fortunate."

Ningbo: Seizure of Smuggled Goods at Shenshi Bridge 98

Shen Yongfa, the former village head of Shenshi Bridge in Cibei, along with his clansmen Shen Wenzhao and Shen Jinzhang, smuggled Japanese goods to Ningbo, evading national taxes. They formed a close-knit group with local porters. Therefore, since last year, they have smuggled countless goods, making it impossible to seize them all. At dawn on the fourth of this month, Shen and others transported a large ship of cigarette paper, rayon, white sugar, kerosene, and other goods from Dalian, worth over 20,000 yuan. The ship docked at the Puhai Beach directly below Shenshi Bridge. The local porters routinely move the goods ashore. However, this time, because there were too many goods, the original agreed-upon porterage fee of one hundred yuan was insufficient. Several ruffians demanded four hundred yuan before they would move the goods. This led to a conflict, almost resulting in violence. Shen Yongfa and others, seeing the dispute unfold and fearing the worst, fled. At this time, over a hundred porters and four hundred private vendors were at a stalemate. One person went to the Guanhaiwei Public Maritime Sub-bureau to report the smuggling and seek a reward. The bureau immediately telegraphed the Zhejiang Maritime Customs Tax Affairs Department, the Zhejiang Maritime Customs Supervision Office, the Yin District Security Command, and the headquarters of the Ministry of Finance's 72nd Tax Police Team. Upon receiving the report, each agency dispatched teams to rush to investigate. They intercepted two hemp sacks of cigarette paper and one barge of white sugar. The remaining smuggled goods and smugglers had all escaped without a trace. The Shenshi Town baojia authorities have been ordered to surrender them within a limited time. As for the rumors circulating that porters and vendors clashed, resulting in multiple deaths and injuries, these are not true.

Bandits in Fenghua Commit Robbery and Murder 99

Xie Awei, a resident of Xixie in Ronghu Street, Sixth District of Fenghua, was a mountain goods vendor. Late last month, he returned home from Ningbo with 160 yuan in paper money. After arriving home, he placed it in the bedside and dresser drawers, preparing to distribute it to various goods suppliers the next day. Unexpectedly, three bandits, armed with wooden-cased guns, broke into Awei's bedroom that night. Awei, seeing the unfavorable situation, immediately fled. His wife, Wang, was seized by the bandits, and after a disagreement, she was fatally shot by the bandits. Their three-year-old daughter, who was being held, suffered a serious leg wound from a bullet. The bandits then looted all the hidden paper money and left. The military police were notified to pursue and arrest the bandits, but they had already fled far away without a trace.
