Local News

Industrial Federation Asks the Ministry to Organize Guangdong's Industry 100

The Chinese General Federation of Industry held a standing committee meeting yesterday. Those in attendance included Guo Shun, Hu Xiyuan, Zhu Gengtao (representing Hu Xiyuan), Cai Shengbai, and Wang Qiyu. The general manager, Qian Chengxu, was present as an observer. The meeting was chaired by Guo Shun. Cai Shengbai proposed ideas for organizing Guangdong's industry, and it was resolved to prepare a document to submit to the Ministry of Industry for review and action.

Petition

Submitting this petition to enumerate opinions on organizing Guangdong Province's industry, respectfully requesting review and adoption. Guangdong is a southern Chinese industrial region, an area where production urgently needs to be developed. In recent years, thanks to the efforts of local individuals, many industries have been actively managed and are showing a thriving atmosphere. However, inappropriate distribution of types of industries or inappropriate decisions on business policies often easily leads to uneven distribution of market areas, reducing production strength. This federation organized the Liangguang Industrial Inspection Group this spring, going to conduct on-site inspections. What was seen and heard led to the deep realization that provincial operation policies, based on the local situation, seem not to be entirely appropriate. Moreover, provincial self-sufficiency and self-supply, if improperly used, can easily lead to economic division, affecting China's entire production. We respectfully enumerate our opinions for your ministry to adopt and implement, as this would be truly convenient for the public. Respectfully submitted to the Minister of Industry, Wu.

Methods

Proposed methods for the Ministry of Industry to organize Guangdong Province's industry are as follows: A. In the current situation, Guangdong's industry should be judged separately based on the advantages of climate and geography to determine the principles of expansion and abandonment. (1) For any industry where there is an abundance of naturally endowed raw materials, unique labor advantages, and the quality of its products can be manufactured to be superior compared to foreign products, this industry should be expanded, such as Guangdong's sugar, hemp spinning, steel refining, and silk reeling factories, etc. (2) For any industry where there are no suitable local raw materials, the skills of the workers are not as good as foreign workers, and the manufacturing cost is higher compared to foreign countries, this industry should be abandoned immediately and should not compete with foreign countries in manufacturing to consume the province's wealth, such as wool spinning and cotton weaving industries. B. Due to differences in economic conditions, the suitability of each industry itself should be studied to determine the principles of provincial operation and private operation. (1) For any industry that requires a large amount of capital or sophisticated technology, is highly international trade-oriented, or is a specialized industry whose products are not in high demand domestically and must be promoted with special efforts, this type of industry should be operated by the state or province. (2) For any industry whose nature is ordinary consumables, is light and easy to produce, and does not require mass production or large amounts of capital, Guangdong's existing industries, in whole or in part, should be classified as privately operated, promoted for development under government guidance, and improved for output, with the government's established experimental institutes, inspection institutes, and standards institutes guiding, organizing, and supervising. Where should what kind of factory be established, and what kind of factory should be state-operated or privately operated? Therefore, central planning is urgently needed. One aspect is to differentiate their trends, and the other aspect is to establish a foundation. Otherwise, it may be that the location and the people are not suitable, thus wasting resources and manpower, or that officials and people operate separately, arousing suspicion of competing for profits, or even that the production and sales areas cannot be unified, leading to chaos. These are all foreseeable facts. If everything is determined by the central government, then there will be a model to follow, and development will proceed rapidly and abundantly according to its program, time, and needs, regardless of whether it is state-operated or province-operated.

Concurrent Acting Social Affairs Bureau Director Pan Gongzhan Assumed Office Yesterday Afternoon, Convening All Staff for Instructions in the Afternoon, Handling the Takeover, No Changes to Bureau Members 101

Shanghai Education Bureau Director Pan Gongzhan, after being ordered by the municipal government to concurrently act as Social Affairs Bureau Director, went to the bureau yesterday at 12:00 PM, accompanied by Social Affairs Bureau Assistant Secretary Chen Baohua, to assume office. After meeting with Social Affairs Bureau Secretary Li Suixian, Second Section Chief Wu Huanru, Third Section Chief Xu Yefu, and Fourth Section Chief Zhang Binghui, he received congratulatory guests such as Luo Qinghua and Ye Jiayu in the reception room, and issued a notice saying, "Shanghai Social Affairs Bureau Notice No. 1: Case received Municipal Government Order No. 1548, which stated, 'Now appoint Education Bureau Director Pan Gongzhan to concurrently act as this city's Social Affairs Bureau Director. This order.' Therefore, I arrived at the bureau today to assume office. In addition to reporting and issuing separate letters, this notice is hereby issued for general knowledge. This notice, Republic of China, June 6, 25th year, Concurrently Acting Director Pan Gongzhan."

Calling Together for Instructions

Director Pan convened all staff in the bureau's auditorium yesterday at 2:00 PM for instructions, the gist of which was: Former Director Wu had a long history of engaging in revolution for the Party and the country, and he was also an old friend of mine for many years. This time, he passed away unfortunately due to overwork and illness, which is very regrettable. Yesterday, the mayor gave me face-to-face instructions, delegating the affairs of the Social Affairs Bureau to me as a concurrent role. As I already have many affairs in the Education Bureau, and the Social Affairs Bureau is also very complicated and demanding, with limited energy, it is difficult to take care of both. I requested the mayor to select other capable people. However, the mayor said that the Social Affairs Bureau is important and cannot be without someone in charge for even a day, and that I had previously held this position, and am a colleague of many years with the people in the bureau. It is my duty to concurrently maintain it, and I cannot refuse. Therefore, I only obey the order to temporarily come to the bureau to preside over it. All facilities in the bureau will remain as they are, and I hope the bureau's secretaries and section chiefs, as well as all colleagues, can uphold the spirit of former Director Wu and continue to work hard. At the same time, I hope the mayor can find capable people as soon as possible to formally take over, so that I can be relieved of my concurrent position and avoid overstepping my bounds.

Handling the Takeover

After Director Pan assumed office yesterday afternoon, he immediately announced Chen Baohua as full-time Assistant Secretary (formerly concurrently Chief of General Affairs), Assistant Secretary Hu Xianqiao (formerly Chief of Accounting), Accounting Section Chief Shen Shouchang (promoted from First Section staff), General Affairs Section Chief Zou Zhixian (promoted from First Section clerk), Dispatch Section Chief Fu Yinian (transferred from Fourth Section staff), First Section Documents Section Chief Shao Tongxuan (transferred from Fourth Section Documents Section Chief), Seal Custodian Shen Baozhen (transferred from Education Bureau First Section clerk), and Fourth Section Documents Section Chief He Jingyuan (promoted from First Section statistician and translator). There were no other changes. The new chiefs of the Accounting, General Affairs, and Dispatch sections immediately took over, and reported to the municipal government.

Deadline for Handling Backlogged Cases

Director Pan immediately issued an order at 3:00 PM yesterday, instructing Secretary Li Suixian to relay to First Section Chief Zhou Renlong, Second Section Chief Wu Huanru, Third Section Chief Xu Yefu, and Fourth Section Chief Zhang Binghui, to order their respective sections to complete at least half of the cases they are handling by August 15th, and to complete all cases by the end of August. If there are special reasons that make it impossible to complete them, they should state their reasons.

Baoshan County Dike Works: No Worries About Autumn Floods, Temporary Emergency Engineering Established, Rushing to Repair Hurricane Damage 103

According to the Xin Xin News Agency, Baoshan County is located on the coast, connecting Shanghai and Taicang counties, and is in the path of the confluence of the East Sea, Yellow Sea, and Yangtze River. The seawall project is the most important area in Jiangnan. Every autumn, the tides are especially strong. If it encounters a storm, the impact will be even greater. Last year, the Jiangsu Province Jiangnan Water Conservancy Engineering Office prepared for flood prevention work in a relatively thorough manner. However, due to funding constraints, before universal repairs were made, emphasis was still placed on emergency work. Currently, the Xiaosabei, Chenhuabin, and Wuyuedun sections all have temporary emergency engineering equipment such as sack filling and stone throwing to prevent any accidents. Therefore, the flood prevention work is relatively thorough. This year's autumn floods should be free from danger. The hurricane on the 3rd of this month struck Japan from the East Sea, with Wusongkou directly in the hurricane's left wing. Therefore, at that time, the wind and rain were violent, and the sea waves were turbulent and abnormal, causing slight damage to the dike works in various sections of the county. Five or six places in the Shidong section were destroyed by the waves. Zhang Mingjing, the county magistrate of the county, went to each section to conduct a detailed inspection the day before yesterday, accompanied by Secretary Bai Mingdao and Third Section Chief Qi Yunzhong. He supervised the Dike Works Office to repair the places that were slightly cracked, and is currently sending additional workers to rush the repairs on the collapsed sections of Shidong.

The country will be fortunate. Also, the association sent letters to various public groups in this city, briefly stating that Japan has violated international law and is establishing a consulate in Chengdu. In addition to requesting that the Ministry of Foreign Affairs negotiate seriously, we also hope to advocate unanimously to maintain sovereignty.

The Xin Sheng News Agency reporter paid a special visit to Wang at his private residence on Yuyuan Road yesterday to inquire about the situation. At that time, Kong only urged him to go north and did not express any other opinions.

Employees of the Shanghai factory who did not wish to follow were given severance pay and dismissed. Only a few cadres were retained to handle the winding-up affairs. All design and guidance will be carried out after Director Zhou arrives in Hankou. Zhou is scheduled to travel by ship from Shanghai next week to carry out the factory restoration work.

The Flour Exchange Abolishes Price Limits from Yesterday; January Futures Open for Trading 113

The Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs, due to the soaring and plummeting prices of the Flour Exchange last month, and the unprecedented increase in trading volume, which clearly indicated speculation by certain elements, imposed price limits twice, on July 8th and July 18th, to restrict such activities. Recently, trading volume has decreased from over 12.4 million bags to over 5.1 million bags. The Exchange applied to the Bureau of Social Affairs to abolish the price limits, which was approved. The price limits were abolished yesterday, and January futures opened for trading.

Prices Rise Slightly

Trading Volume Not High. After implementation yesterday, opening market prices were: August at $3.14, September at $3.18, October at $3.25, November at $3.28, December at $3.31, and January at $3.40. Compared to the previous day, August rose by 6 cents, September rose by 9 cents, October rose by 10 cents, and November rose by 10 cents. Trading volume remained low.

Additional Margin Call for Sellers

Because the Exchange abolished price limits and prices rose, it announced yesterday that sellers must provide additional margin. Australian Aviator Flies to Europe via Russia; Negotiations Underway 114

Mr. Keith Hilder, an Australian amateur aviator, flew from Fuzhou to Longhua Airport at 2:40 PM on the 5th. He originally planned to fly to Nanjing yesterday to visit the Soviet Russian Ambassador to China, Mr. Bogomolov, to request the Soviet Russian government to allow him to fly to Europe via Russian territory. However, after learning that Mr. Bogomolov was resting in Qingdao, he cancelled the trip and invited Sir Brenan, the British Consul-General in Shanghai, to visit Mr. Spilvanyk, the Soviet Russian Consul-General in Shanghai, to discuss methods of flying over Russian territory. Mr. Hilder's trip to Europe requires passing through Manchuria and Soviet Russia. The Manchurian side has already given its permission, but the Russian side has not yet agreed, citing military reasons for not approving. Mr. Hilder believes that it may be possible to negotiate a detour route that does not interfere with military affairs. However, according to experts in this city, detours are very dangerous and this should be carefully considered.

Deadline for Supplementary Registration Approaching; Cracked Down on Opium Dens and Smokers; 88 People Arrested in the Old North Gate Area 115

88 People Arrested in the Old North Gate Area Since the Municipal Public Security Bureau began accepting supplementary registration of opium smokers on May 10th of this year, all unregistered smokers have been allowed to register. The deadline of August 10th is fast approaching. If anyone still intends to evade registration, once the deadline has passed, any unregistered smokers found will be sent to the Songhu Garrison Headquarters and punished according to the anti-opium laws, without leniency. In recent days, the various branches have received many requests for supplementary registration. Dada Steamship Company to Develop Shipping in Northern Jiangsu 116

According to the Xin Xin News Agency, the Dada Steamship Company in this city, which owns the Dada, Dahe, Daqing, and Guangxiang ships, operates services between Shanghai and various ports along the Yangtze River, including Tongzhou, Yangzhou, and Chongming. To facilitate transportation in northern Jiangsu and develop shipping, the company has reorganized the river vessel bureaus in northern Jiangsu and implemented joint river transport on six routes: Shanghai-Yangzhou-Tongzhou-Taizhou-Haian-Dongtai. Mr. Zai Xianglun and Yi Yingfu, directors of the Nantong Tianshenggang Port, have been appointed to be responsible for handling the matter. The takeover of six vessels operating on the inland rivers, including the Da Xiang, Da Xun, Da He, and Da Jin, as well as four barges, has been completed. The Tangzha Vessel Bureau has been abolished and is now under the unified management of the company. Two vessels will be dedicated to the Dongtai-Haian route, and the other four will be dedicated to the Tonghai (Nantong to Haian) route. The first step is to implement joint transportation between Nantong and Haian, and then decide on the joint transportation of Huai'an, Dongtai, and Taizhou, to connect with the Shanghai-Yangzhou and other outer river routes. Northern Jiangsu is known for its abundant cotton and wheat production. After the implementation of joint transportation, products can be directly transported from the production areas to Shanghai for sale, avoiding the complexity of transshipment and reducing transportation costs significantly. This will greatly facilitate transportation in northern Jiangsu.

Large Number of Tax Police Stationed on Daishan Island; Fishermen Dare Not Venture Out to Sea to Fish; Zhuang Songfu and Others Telegraph the Ningbo Hometown Association for Assistance to Recall Tax Police, Soothe Refugees, and Eliminate Hidden Dangers 118

The Ningbo Shanghai Hometown Association telegraphed the Salt Administration of the Ministry of Finance and the Zhejiang Provincial Government, stating, "According to a telegram from Zhuang Songfu, Wang Boxian, Lin Shouting, Mi Youzan, Chen Zhan'ao, Lin Hairui, Shen Yiben, and others from Fenghua, (the above is omitted). This is a decisive matter for the Daishan Island in Dinghai County. Due to the salt authorities' failure to adapt to the situation and lead by example in handling the change in fisheries and the consolidation of salt supervision, and due to the various forms of harassment and extortion by the tax police, the disaster of July 13th was triggered. The detailed circumstances have been reported by Commissioner Zhao of the Yin County District. We invite you to examine the reports, which are widely published in newspapers. We, Zhuang Songfu and others, will not go into unnecessary detail. Those who initiated the incident are undoubtedly guilty, but those who are law-abiding should be clearly distinguished. The livelihood of fishermen along the coast of eastern Zhejiang depends on the spring and autumn fishing seasons. Now is the beginning of the autumn season. Fishing firms are collecting capital and issuing loans, fishing factories are manufacturing and selling fishing nets, and fishing boats are venturing out to sea to fish. However, the salt authorities of Daishan have greatly increased the number of tax police, several times the usual amount. They indiscriminately threaten and intimidate fishermen and merchants from other regions who come to the island, and search ships. The atmosphere of terror has not been dispelled, and there is concern about being falsely accused. People are anxious and do not know what to do. Therefore, good fishermen dare not venture out to sea to fish, and fishing firms are hesitant to proceed. Their livelihoods are cut off, and they are forced into a difficult situation. If they take risks, the consequences are unimaginable. The most important task for the aftermath is not to arrest the perpetrators, but to reassure the good people. To reassure the good people, the tax police must first be withdrawn so that fishermen can safely venture out to sea and fishing firms can operate as usual. Then, the judicial authorities can arrest and punish the perpetrators, and those who were coerced should be pardoned. It is not appropriate to implicate too many people. This is in line with the principle of eliminating violence and reassuring the good people, and of giving the benefit of the doubt to the accused. It is also a way to protect the livelihoods of fishermen and eliminate hidden dangers. Zhuang Songfu and others feel that the situation is critical and cannot remain silent. Therefore, they dare to take the risk of speaking out and asking for assistance. We hope that your association will care for the homeland and speak out for justice. We are sending this telegram in the hope that you will all advocate for this. Fisheries and fishermen will be fortunate. The details of the unfortunate incident in Daishan are detailed in the telegrams that our association has sent. According to the telegram, the local authorities have dispatched a large number of tax police to be stationed, and the people are afraid of the past and deeply fear that they will take the opportunity to retaliate. They do not dare to work and live in peace. If this continues, the local area will be in a dire situation. The fellow villagers advocate that the key to the aftermath is not to arrest the perpetrators but to reassure the good people, which coincides with the views of our association. In light of the situation described in the telegram, we are urgently sending a telegram to request your review and support in order to eliminate hidden dangers and stabilize the people's hearts. We eagerly await your instructions. Qi Qiaqing, Chairman of the Ningbo Shanghai Hometown Association."

National Match United Company to Be Officially Established in October; Match Manufacturers to Voluntarily Control Production and Sales; More Than 80 Chinese and Japanese Factories Support 119

According to the Shen Shi News Agency, match manufacturing is a light industry, and a small-scale match factory can be operated with a capital of four to five thousand yuan. Therefore, since 1933, many new factories have been established. By the second half of 1934, due to overproduction and pressure from foreign forces and competition from fellow manufacturers, the entire Chinese match industry was in a state of bankruptcy and unable to struggle.

Chinese and Japanese Promote Controlled Matches

On January 9th of this year, Chinese and Japanese match factories jointly proposed to establish a match united association, with match manufacturers voluntarily controlling production and sales. Most manufacturers expressed their approval of this principle. In March of this year, the Ministry of Industry approved the organization. For several months, the leaders of Chinese and Japanese manufacturers, Liu Hongsheng and Ueda, have been working tirelessly, and by the end of last month, the organization began to take shape.

More Than 80 Manufacturers Join

More than 80 match manufacturers have joined the United Company, including over 70 Chinese factories from 22 provinces, including Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Guangdong, Shandong, Hunan, Sichuan, Shanxi, Hebei, Anhui, Guangxi, Jiangxi, and Hubei. The Japanese side has joined with eight factories from Beiping, Tianjin, Qingdao, and other places. The American-owned Meiguang Match Company in this city, after the earnest persuasion of both Chinese and Japanese sides, is also planning to join.

Continuous Negotiations on Implementation Matters

The Shen Shi News Agency reporter learned that Chinese and Japanese match merchants, in order to carry out the United Company, have been continuously represented by Liu Hongsheng, Xu Zhiyi, and other manufacturers, along with representatives from the Japanese factories, including Takawa, Kanayama, Hirajima, and Taniguchi, and secretary Ueda, negotiating the organization of controlled matches. It is reported that the name of the National Match United Association will be changed to National Match United Company.

Establishment Expected in Mid-October

As for the organization of the company, Liu Hongsheng will be the manager, and eight directors and two supervisors will be elected. The capital will be 5 million yuan, with Chinese merchants accounting for 75%, or 3.75 million yuan, and Japanese merchants accounting for 25%, or 1.25 million yuan. It is expected that the company will be officially established in mid-October of this year.

State-Owned China Merchants Steam Navigation Company Report on Reorganization (Continued) C. Personnel Reorganization 121

(1) Qualification Examination of Employees of the General and Branch Bureaus After the reorganization of the Bureau, the organizational structure changed, and the existing number of employees was excessive and had to be reduced. In order to eliminate the inferior and retain the superior and improve efficiency, a qualification examination for employees of the General Bureau was conducted in February of this year. In late February, an order was issued announcing the qualified employees who would be retained, and they were assigned to work in their original sections and units as section members and assistants. Those who failed the examination were given severance pay in accordance with the approved methods and dismissed. The qualification examination for personnel of the branch bureaus was also held in March. Those who had not taken the examination in the various bureaus and offices were allowed to take a supplementary examination at the Bureau in late April. Those who passed the examination were all announced in May and retained as clerks and assistants in accordance with the approved number. Those who failed the examination were also given severance pay and dismissed. (2) Implementation of Inspections for Shipboard Employees It has been found that shipboard employees often suffer from serious illnesses, physical disabilities, and mental decline, which has a significant impact on work efficiency and public health. Unless inspections are carried out, there is no way to distinguish between good and bad. Except for the engine room staff who have passed the qualification examination by the Maritime Affairs Bureau and are exempted from re-examination, all other shipboard staff are subject to inspection. For example, service staff (formerly tea attendants) and boiler stokers, as well as business staff, have all been examined in turn, and measures have been established. In addition to retaining those who are qualified, those who suffer from serious illnesses or have bad habits have been dismissed or suspended with pay for a period of time to receive treatment and return to service. This inspection work was carried out by doctors assigned by the Shanghai Municipal Health Bureau and assisted by doctors from the Chinese Red Cross Hospital. After this inspection, not only did the employees themselves become more vigilant, but the efficiency of their work also indirectly increased, resulting in considerable intangible benefits. (3) Implementation of Employee Training In order to train employees' physique, increase their knowledge, and implement military training, the Bureau established an Employee Training Committee on May 29th of this year in accordance with the Ministry's order to be responsible for the work. All training plans and academic subjects, as well as schedules, were prepared in detail. Training was first carried out for service staff on the various ships, starting in July. Subsequently, training will be carried out in turn for other employees, such as dock porters and watchmen, until all employees have completed training. (4) Promotion of the New Life Movement It has been found that the old customs and bad habits of the Yangtze River ships are deeply ingrained. In the past, the Bureau's Yangtze River ships were not able to completely eliminate them. Now, the New Life Movement Promotion Association has dispatched two members to each of the Bureau's Yangtze River ships to guide the New Life Movement. Matters stipulated in the New Life Movement are being implemented, with particular emphasis on hygiene, cleanliness, work order, and convenience for passengers. It is expected that the old habits of the Yangtze River ships will be completely eradicated, and the New Life Movement regulations will be fully implemented. (5) Reorganization of Ticket Inspection Matters The Bureau's ships have been required to sell tickets on shore since the reorganization. Therefore, more attention should be paid to ticket inspection on board to prevent abuses and omissions. Currently, in addition to the Bureau's original ticket inspectors performing their duties, the Ministry has also assigned one ticket inspector per ship to assist in the inspection. Since implementation, not only has it been beneficial to the increase in business and passenger revenue, but also the other shipboard affairs have been inspected and improved. (6) Production and Issuance of Employee Uniforms, Badges, and Service Certificates

In order to make it easier for passengers to identify employees and to facilitate work assessment, the Bureau has produced and issued uniforms and badges for the service staff on each ship, and ordered them to wear them. In addition to registering all employees of the Bureau, branch offices, and ships, each employee is issued a service certificate. The certificate states the employee's name, origin, age, position, etc., and includes a photograph of the employee. The employee's service record and commendation and punishment records are recorded by the supervisor and reported to the Bureau for filing. The certificate must be carried at all times while on duty for inspection. The Bureau has now paid for the production of the certificates, which will be printed soon and issued separately. (7) Military Police Escorting Ships Since the reorganization of the Bureau, it has been ordered to dispatch military police to escort the ships and crack down on passengers without tickets. Since implementation, it has been quite effective. At the same time, except for special circumstances, wooden fences and rain shelters have been installed at the wharves of each port for ticket sales in order to facilitate inspection and convenience for passengers. (8) Restricting Vendors from Boarding Ships Vendors often board the ships at various ports along the Yangtze River to sell goods, causing a great deal of noise and affecting the peace and order on board. In order to ensure cleanliness, peace, and order on board, the Bureau has restricted vendors from boarding ships. Each branch bureau has been ordered to implement this measure and maintain the principle of not allowing vendors to board ships. Since implementation, not only has order on board been maintained, but also the number of quarrels and disputes has been reduced. (9) Holding Registration for Porters Dock porters have never been subject to management, which has had various adverse effects on the transportation of goods and luggage. In order to facilitate management, the Bureau has formulated plans to hold a registration for porters and ordered each branch bureau to comply. Currently, the branch bureaus have either not held registration due to the lack of porters, or have had to develop separate measures for handling the situation. (End)

After a Smoker Quits: The Problem of Punishment for Having the Addiction Without the Vice. The Shanghai County Government Explains Following Provincial Order, Stating That if One Has Already Quitted, It is Difficult to Impose Criminal Responsibility. 122

Yesterday, the Shanghai County Government received an order from the Jiangsu-Zhejiang Provincial Government which stated: “Regarding the case where it was previously reported to the Chairman of the Military Affairs Commission and concurrently Director-General of the Anti-Opium Bureau, Order No. 1574, based on the submission from Jian Minglong, Chairman of the Wujiang County Chinese Medicine Association, that smokers who have quit are being tested and found to have the addiction without the vice, yet are still being sentenced, which is a great loss of legal and moral fairness. Please order a correction, and investigate and report whether this province sentences smokers who have quit and are found to have the addiction without the vice, or whether there are other handling methods, for verification and approval.”

The response stated, "Regarding the matter of sentencing those found to have the addiction without the vice after testing, there is no definite standard, and we are experiencing difficulties during review. We request instructions on how to proceed."

The explanation is as follows: "Regarding initial opium use and initial drug use, if one has voluntarily quit or voluntarily entered a rehabilitation program before being discovered, even within the implementation period of the Anti-Opium Law, according to Article 16 of the Implementing Rules of the Anti-Opium Law, they 'may be exempted from punishment.' According to Article 291 of the Criminal Procedure Law, a notice of exemption from punishment may be issued. However, since the Provisional Regulations for Punishing Offenses of Opium and Drug Suppression do not have this provision, in the aforementioned circumstances, unless the prosecution has been reduced due to the statute of limitations, a decision not to prosecute should be made according to Article 231, Paragraph 2 of the Criminal Procedure Law. However, they may only be granted exemption from punishment, non-prosecution, reduced punishment, or probation according to Articles 61, 293, and 232 of the Criminal Procedure Law, and Articles 59, 63, or 74 of the Criminal Law. In the case of smokers who have quit and have the addiction without the vice, the initial offense of opium use and the initial offense of drug use, if voluntarily quit or entered rehabilitation before discovery, are not expressly punishable by law and cannot be convicted. This has been repeatedly explained in previous cases. Although it cannot be determined when those with the addiction without the vice stopped using, it is clear that they voluntarily quit before being discovered. Therefore, it is difficult to impose criminal responsibility."

Therefore, in addition to issuing separate orders, this order is for the county magistrate to comply with.

Kidnapping Case of Xu Wenliang: Two More Kidnappers Apprehended; Awaiting Recovery and Interrogation of the Two Wounded Kidnappers 123

Xu Wenliang, a Cantonese man and manager of the oil department of the Mei Foo Company, residing at No. 1305 Yuyuan Road, Shanghai West, was suddenly invaded by seven armed kidnappers at around 3:00 AM on July 14th. They robbed the house and kidnapped Xu Wenliang. Subsequently, the Chengdu Road Police Department successively apprehended nine men and women, including Cao Chunbao, Lu Laisheng, Zhang Heshang, Zhang Xushi, and others, and rescued the hostage Xu Wenliang. They were sent to the First Special Court. The interrogation revealed that defendants Cao Chunbao and Shen Tingyan were injured and in the hospital, so the hearing was adjourned to a later date.

As reported in this newspaper, at around 9:00 PM the night before, Chinese Detective Feng Baishun and Detective Sun Wenxi of the Chengdu Road Police Department, together with the Municipal Public Security Bureau, apprehended Lu Zhifeng (nicknamed "Headless Ghost A-Liu"), a native of Ningbo and accomplice in the case, in Yanjiabao, Pudong. Yesterday morning, Du Haisheng (aka "Shaoxing A-Da"), also from Ningbo, was apprehended at the New New Inn at No. 138 Rue des Soeurs, French Concession. Both were brought back to the police station for detention.

Yesterday morning, they were sent to the Eighth Criminal Division of the First Special Court. Zhang Tianyin, the police lawyer, stated the case, saying that defendants Chen and Du had admitted to participating in the kidnapping of Xu Wenliang at the police station. As Cao Chunbao and Shen Tingyan had not yet recovered from their injuries, he requested permission for indefinite detention. After Judge Tan Xinzhen briefly questioned Chen and Du, he granted permission for detention and ordered that Cao Chunbao and others be interrogated together after their recovery.

The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Xin Jiangtian steamer collided with the Jin Wanli sailboat at 4:00 AM on February 18th in the Y窩沙 waters outside Wusong Port. Invention of Reed Pulp Paper Making Material; Submitted to the Ministry for Patent 133

Bian Liangbo, a native of Huai'an, Jiangsu, realized that the purchase of foreign wood pulp for paper making materials resulted in a great loss of rights. He personally visited the production area of reeds and conducted investigations and research, inventing a kind of reed pulp for paper making materials. He previously applied to the Ministry of Industry for a patent, but it was not approved due to omissions. He is now reapplying to the Ministry of Industry, stating: "Submitting to supplement the omissions in the previous submission, requesting another review and special patent approval. The reed pulp invented by the applicant has also been tested by experts, and its nature and function are no less than that of foreign wood pulp. Recently, a detailed investigation was conducted in the reed production area, and it was found that there are as many as 3 million dan produced annually. If it is used for pulp making, 1.5 million shi can be obtained. To recover the lost rights, a joint venture has been agreed to set up a paper mill. If the patent part is not favorably considered, the future of the joint venture will collapse. The loss of personal spirit is limited, but the outflow of national rights is infinite. Furthermore, the Ministry has specially granted patents for the recently invented multi-filament light bulbs and three-way light bulbs. Considering their operation methods, they are nothing more than button rotations and the contact relationship with filaments. They were recognized as inventions because of their different characteristics, not the patent of the method. In accordance with Article 15 of the Provisional Regulations for Encouraging Industrial Technology, I am supplementing the reasons and submitting a document for review, hoping that you will grant special patent approval. It would be a great kindness. Respectfully submitted to the Ministry of Industry."

New Regulations for Licensing Public and Private Rickshaws and Rickshaw Pullers Announced 134

The conditions for licensing public rickshaws and rickshaw pullers (public and private) have recently been revised and announced by the Municipal Council. The key points of the revision are described below:

The most important new regulations for licensing public rickshaw pullers are that licenses and armbands must not be lent to others. In addition, it is stipulated that if a rickshaw puller leaves Shanghai for more than half a month, the license and armband should be returned to the licensing office for temporary storage to prevent misuse by others. On the other hand, the rickshaw owner or contractor should be notified so that they can find a temporary replacement.

For private rickshaw pullers, the license and armband must not be lent to others. Furthermore, the rickshaw owner's license number and name must be noted on the rickshaw puller's license for frequent inspection. A new clause has also been added to the public rickshaw license, which aims to distinguish the rent paid by the rickshaw puller to the rickshaw owner from other items of money so that it is easier to investigate abuses such as overcharging rent. In addition, there are strict regulations regarding the installation of rickshaw lamps, the rickshaw puller's uniform, and raincoats. The name and address of the rickshaw contractor must also be reported to the Municipal Council by the rickshaw owner at any time.

Liu Huizhen's Case Against Yang Zhongfen; Two Witnesses Interrogated Yesterday; Both Claim Yang and Liu Have a Relationship; The Court Ordered the Verdict to be Announced Next Thursday 136

Yang Zhongfen, a Fujianese man and secretary of the board of directors of the Zhongnan Bank, was sued in the First Special Court by Liu Huizhen, a woman from Suzhou, through lawyers Huang Xiubo and others, accusing Yang of seduction and abandonment of their biological son A-Li, and requesting payment of living and educational expenses of 20,000 yuan. The court repeatedly held hearings, and the Zhenru Forensic Research Institute identified that the blood types of Yang Zhongfen and Liu Huizhen were both O, meaning they could have children with the O blood type like A-Li. However, because two important witnesses did not arrive, the hearing was rescheduled.

Yesterday afternoon, Judge Zhong Qing presided over the case in the Second Criminal Court and continued the interrogation. The witnesses were all present. Wang Yingzeng, the landlord of No. 3 Hongxing Lane, Aiwenyi Road, testified that Yang Zhongfen came to rent the upstairs room in April of last year, giving him a card stating that the monthly rent was 18 yuan and that he would live with his family. Later, a woman (the plaintiff) came with him, her abdomen swollen. They lived there for a month and then moved out. He presented the card to the court. Zhou Guiying, a female doctor from the Kemei Obstetrics Hospital on Xiafei Road and a native of Ningbo, testified that she and Dr. Mao went to No. 39 Shengda Lane, Shengmuyuan Road, to deliver Liu Huizhen's baby on September 15th of last year. Yang Zhongfen was also present, and Yang paid the delivery fee of 21 yuan. Yang and Liu also came together when registering. Fang Pinzhen, a female registration clerk at the Kemei Hospital, testified that Yang Zhongfen and Liu came together when registering. She presented the registration book to the court, explaining that Yang instructed her to write Liu's last name on the registration book.

When questioned, the defendant Yang Zhongfen denied the above three testimonies. The court, seeing that the facts were clear, ordered the debate to begin. The lawyers for both parties debated for a long time. Judge Zhong ordered that the verdict be announced next Thursday.

Female Flower Gambling Boss Fined, Payment in Three Installments: Lu Laoqi Still Claims She Cannot Borrow Money, Willing to Serve Jail Time Instead, Request Denied 146

Lu Wenying, the female flower gambling boss also known as Lu Laoqi, was wanted for two years based on a warrant issued by the French Concession Police to the Special Court No. 2. Lu hid in the Hujia Pavilion of Fahua, West Shanghai. Last winter, she came to Shanghai and went to the Wusheng Hall on Xiyanglou to offer incense to Buddha. She was discovered by the French Concession Police at a friend's house surnamed Yang in Yuren Lane on Yunnan Road. The French Concession Police dispatched detectives together with the Laozha Police to arrest her and transfer her to the Special Court No. 2. The police attorney of the police department filed a public prosecution based on the crime of gambling. After the trial, she was sentenced to two years in prison and fined 1,500 yuan. Lu refused to accept the sentence and appealed to the High Court No. 3. The judgment reduced the prison term by six months, but the fine was still executed according to the original judgment. However, Lu was released on bail of 6,000 yuan after the first trial. After the appeal judgment was finalized, she still claimed to be ill and requested a postponement of execution. The High Court No. 3 issued a warrant to arrest Lu and send her to the Special Prison No. 2 to serve her prison term. A few days ago, Zhu, the acting criminal court judge of the High Court No. 3, held a court session to bring Lu to court and execute the fine, as previously reported in this newspaper. However, Lu was unable to raise funds in prison, so no amount of the fine has been paid. Yesterday morning, acting Judge Zhu held a court session again to bring her to court and continue the execution of the fine. Lu still claimed that she was unable to raise funds and was willing to serve jail time instead. The judge announced that after the court session, the court received an anonymous letter stating that fines were converted to jail time in other cases. However, your case is different from other cases, so it cannot be converted. The court is now giving you a deadline to pay the fine in three installments. The first installment must be paid within ten days, otherwise the court will have its own way to deal with it. Lu heard the announcement, lowered her head, and remained silent. As a result, the court ordered the bailiffs to take Lu away and send her back to prison to serve her sentence.

Upstream Floodwaters Discharge Downstream, Middle Reaches of the Yangtze River Surge, Yichang Water Level Suddenly Rises Fourteen Feet, Hankou Water Level Breaks Thirty Feet Downstream 154

Due to heavy rains in the upper reaches of the Yangtze River, the water level at ports such as Chongqing rose sharply. According to a Chongqing dispatch on the 5th, the water level has receded. However, according to a reporter from the Datong News Agency, the Shanghai Customs Office learned yesterday morning that the middle and lower reaches of the Yangtze River have been affected by the discharge of floodwaters from the upper reaches. The details are recorded below:

Water Level Surge

According to a reporter from the Datong News Agency, the Shanghai Customs Office learned yesterday morning that the water level in the middle reaches of the Yangtze River has suddenly increased due to the discharge of floodwaters from the upper reaches. The water level in Yichang has suddenly increased by fourteen feet in the past four or five days. The customs office's water level reports from Yichang from the 1st to the 5th are as follows: The water level in Yichang on the 1st was 24 feet 7 inches, on the 2nd it was 23 feet 7 inches, on the 3rd it was 23 feet 4 inches, on the 4th it suddenly rose to 28 feet 4 inches (a sharp increase of 5 feet), and on the 5th the rise was even more rapid, with the water level increasing to 37 feet 5 inches (a sharp increase of 8 feet 9 inches). As of the 6th, the customs office had not yet received a report on the water level.

Downstream Gradually Affected

As for the water level in Hankou in the lower reaches of the Yangtze River, the customs office's record is still the report from the 1st of this month, with a quantity of 31 feet 2 inches (at the end of last month it was only 29 feet 9 inches), which is also a slight increase. As the floodwaters from Yichang discharge downstream in recent days, it is feared that the water level will continue to increase. It is also learned that the climate in the Yangtze River basin has remained unstable in recent days, so the customs office is paying attention again and will determine appropriate navigation facilities based on the development of the flood situation in the next few days.

Zhou Mengyun Lectures on Telescopic Abacus, More Than 200 Attendees 156

Zhou Mengyun, a researcher of abacus calculation, invented the telescopic abacus, but citizens are not yet clear about its structure and use. Therefore, at 9 AM yesterday, he publicly exhibited it at the lecture hall of the Mass Education Center on Wenmiao Road. Mr. Zhou lectured on the origins and learning methods of abacus calculation, as well as the motivation and process of inventing the telescopic abacus. More than 200 people attended the lecture. A copy of Zhou's "New Theory of Abacus" was distributed on the spot for research. The telescopic abacus publicly exhibited yesterday morning is characterized by its non-fixed columns, which can be extended to 18 columns and reduced to 15 columns, 11 columns, or 9 columns. There are symbols on the crossbeam for decimal points. During calculation, it can be moved at will, making it easy to identify the position of integers and decimals. It can also be folded and packed in a box, making it very convenient to carry.

Eleventh Olympic Games 1936

Our National Football Team Loses to England Two to Zero, 1500m Hurdles Creates World Record, Our National Basketball Team Plays Japan Today 191

Our newspaper's exclusive dispatch from Berlin, 6th: Our national football team fought England today. The battle was exceptionally fierce. The first half ended in a 0-0 draw, with neither side scoring. In the second half, England scored two goals. Our team lost 0-2.

(Berlin) On the morning of the fifth day of the World Games, the stadium held no fewer than 30,000 spectators. By 10 a.m., the stadium was already overcrowded. The weather was still cold, with dense clouds covering the sky. Fortunately, it did not rain. The audience was most excited about today's 1,500-meter final. New Zealand's Lovelock broke the world record of 3 minutes 48.8 seconds set by America's Glenn Cunningham in 1934 with a time of 3 minutes 47 seconds. Second place went to American general Cunningham with 3 minutes 48.4 seconds, also a new world record. The previous World Games champion Beccali (Italy), with 3 minutes 49.2 seconds, also shortened his own previous Olympic record of 3 minutes 51.2 seconds, making it a valuable achievement for the Games. Also, in today's hurdles semi-final, American athlete Towns set a new world record with 14.1 seconds, shortening the old record by one-tenth of a second, created by American athlete Payton. (6th, Kuomintang Hai Tong News Agency dispatch)

(Kuomintang Hai Tong News Agency) Berlin, August 6th: The German press has reported in detail on the success of American athlete Owens. When a reporter asked Owens about the secret to his success, Owens replied, "I live the life of a sportsman. Is this the secret to success?" German long jump athlete Long, who won second place in the long jump this time, said, "Owens only jumps as far as he needs to. If he meets an opponent, he can jump over eight meters. During the 200-meter final, there was a favorable wind, and the wind was quite strong. Owens was assisted by Aeolus. However, he is good at sprinting. After the start, he was always in the lead. His winning the championship was as easy as taking something out of a pocket. Owens' status as the number one sprinter was further confirmed in this final.

(Kuomintang Hai Tong News Agency) Berlin, August 5th: American black sprinter Owens broke the World Games record again in today's 200-meter final. This is the third gold medal Owens has won at the Games. (1) Owens (USA) 20.7 seconds, (2) Robinson (USA) 21.1 seconds, (3) Osendarp (Netherlands) 21.3 seconds.

Owens' success in the 100 meters and long jump has become the focus of attention at this World Games. His fame will never cease to be heroic in sports history. In the 200-meter final, Owens' heroic posture was once again presented to an audience of 100,000. From the start, Owens was in the lead, overwhelming the crowd. European athlete Osendarp made a final effort to make up some distance, but ultimately could not match the American athlete in second place.

The previous World Games record was 21.1 seconds, set by American black athlete Tolan in 1932. The current world record is 20.6 seconds, set by America's Locke in 1926.

Owens won three gold medals in track and field events at the Eleventh World Games, which is unprecedented. Therefore, this alone has become a glorious page in the history of world sports. Finland's Nurmi won four gold medals at the World Games, but Nurmi's were the total achievements of three World Games, so they are different from those won by Owens in one Games.

Pole Vault Final Results, 4.35 Meters, American Athlete Meadows Sets Games Record 196

Havas dispatch from Berlin, 5th: The pole vault final began at 3 p.m. today and lasted until 9 p.m., lasting six hours. Later, it was already late, and the stadium lights were all on, illuminating the stadium as if it were daytime, so that the athletes could still show their skills in the evening. As a result, the champion was an American athlete, followed by Nishida and Ooe. The score was four feet twenty-five. The two competed with American athletes Meadows, Gralund, and Sefton. At first, they were evenly matched, but when it was up to two feet twenty-five, Gralund was exhausted and could not pass. When it was up to 4.35 meters, Sefton and the two Japanese athletes also failed to pass. Only Meadows had the remaining courage to sell, and jumped over it. When it was up to 4.45 meters, Meadows did not pass either, but the difference was only a fraction of an inch, so 4.35 meters was the final score he achieved.

According to the Games record, it was 4.3 meters. 5.1932 was created by American Miller and has been broken. As for the world record of 4.37 meters, it was also created by Gralund (USA) in 1930.

Dōmei News Agency dispatch from Berlin, 5th: The rankings for the pole vault final are below.

This final, held at 4 p.m. on the afternoon of the 5th, was indeed a battle for supremacy between Japan and the United States. When the height reached 4.35 meters, only four athletes from Japan and the United States remained, competing for the final victory in the twilight. American Meadows failed in the first attempt, but jumped over it on the second try, setting a new Games record. Japanese Nishida, Ooe, and American Sefton all failed to cross after three attempts. The supremacy was therefore given to American Meadows. The 40,000 spectators in the stands applauded thunderously and did not stop for a while. After that, the three selected athletes competed for second place. As a result, American Sefton was disqualified, and the two Japanese athletes occupied the second and third places. However, the time had passed the time for the game to stop, and the sun had set. The referees announced the end of the game and judged Sefton in fourth place and Gralund in fifth place.

World Games Athlete Delegation's Accompanying Journal (Letter 5) Special Correspondent of the Central News Agency, Feng Youzhen 209

(2)(6) A Scene in the Red Sea: Tragedy

On the night of the 13th, the mail ship passed through the Gulf of Aden and sailed into the Red Sea. The azure seawater was so calm that it was almost without a ripple. After everyone had suffered through the stormy waves, arriving at such a peaceful state was truly very comfortable.

The Red Sea is over 1,100 miles long, 200 miles at its widest point, and only 16 miles at its narrowest. Both shores are visible. The southern shore of the Red Sea is the Arabian Desert, and the northern shore is the African Desert. Amidst the evaporation of these two great deserts, the climate is extremely hot. It is said that it is because of the heat that it was given the name "Red Sea," but it has absolutely nothing to do with the color of the seawater.

On the morning of the 14th, the sky was azure and clear, and the sun blazed fiercely. Canvas awnings were erected on the deck, but they still could not resist the scorching heat of the sun. The electric fans in the smoking room were turned on at full speed, but even sitting inside, bright beads of sweat flowed like a spring. The breeze blowing over the sea was filled with heat. Everything felt a bit scorching to the touch. In the afternoon, we arrived at Massawa. The ship stopped, and the wind ceased. The heat from the desert evaporated, causing even more headaches and mental fatigue. Amidst such heat waves, it was unimaginable that a tragedy would occur. A Dutchman who worked for the Javanese government was retiring and returning home with his wife, son, and daughter. He boarded the ship from Singapore. This gentleman was about 50 years old, weighed 200 pounds, and had a very amiable and approachable demeanor. We had been on the ship together for more than ten days and were very familiar with each other. In particular, his 15-year-old daughter and 13-year-old son, innocent and lively, played very affectionately with everyone. They also lived in the economical second-class cabins, which were even more stifling as they were near the engine room. On the night of the 14th, he went to the deck to cool off and felt a bit unwell. He returned to his room, and not long after, he suddenly passed away. On the morning of the 15th, everyone heard this tragic news and felt extremely saddened and a sense of the fleetingness of life. According to the ship's regulations, if a passenger dies mid-journey, a burial at sea should be held. At 6 p.m. that afternoon, the ship lowered its flag to half-mast and slowed down. The captain, dressed in formal attire, held a simple memorial service for him, and then the body was placed in a wooden box and slowly lowered into the sea. It is said that there were also four workers on the ship who were victims of the heat wave. Their bodies were quietly thrown into the sea, becoming companions to the waves and buried in the bellies of fish.

(2)(7) Impressions of Massawa

At 2 p.m. on the afternoon of the 14th, the ship arrived at Massawa. Although the sun was blazing and sweat poured down our backs, many people still went ashore to sightsee because this place was an important military base during the Italo-Ethiopian War.

Massawa is the capital of Italian Eritrea and its only commercial port. It is located on the Red Sea coast, serving as a vital transportation hub between Europe and Asia, its importance second only to British Aden and French Djibouti. Eritrea was originally part of Abyssinia (Ethiopia) but was later ceded to Italy. Now, Italy uses Eritrea as a base, and even Abyssinia has been completely annexed. When the Italo-Ethiopian War was in progress, Massawa was the key entry point for Italian troops heading to Africa via the northern route. Now that we are here in person, as we witness the hideous and ferocious face of imperialism, we cannot help but think back to our motherland's fragmented rivers and mountains and the hardships and difficulties of our nation's fate. It truly fills us with shock and dismay. As the mail ship approached the coast of Massawa, we saw from afar many warships and merchant ships anchored there. These warships and merchant ships were all Italian because ships from other countries never dock at Massawa. When the mail ship docked, we saw many colored and colorless laborers, under the command of several officers, busily engaged in transportation work. Dozens of transport vehicles were also traveling back and forth frequently. This clearly shows that although the Italo-Ethiopian War has come to an end, military arrangements are still in full swing.

Massawa can be summarized in two phrases: "a desert area, a military stronghold." The entire town is very small, at most comparable to a slightly larger town in our country. It is entirely built on a desert. The houses are very dilapidated, and the climate is extremely hot. We walked through all the streets and only saw a telegraph office (with a post office attached) and less than ten extremely small shops. Apart from residences, all other buildings are for military use.

The streets are dusty, dirty, and unbearably smelly, making one want to vomit. Apart from a few palm trees, there is no other greenery. Such a desolate place seems unworthy of anyone's attachment, but because it is the gateway to Abyssinia, Italy regards it as the source of life. No wonder our country, with its fertile lands for thousands of miles, is coveted by others.

The skin of the natives is as black as the bottom of a pot, and their appearance is ferocious. Compared to them, the Indians are insignificant. Men and women are bare-chested, wearing only a piece of colored cloth around their lower bodies. Under the command of the colorless race, they lead a laborious life like beasts of burden. Their ignorance and lack of knowledge are evident at a glance. Such a nation can only survive independently if no one seeks to slaughter it. I write this not to advocate for imperialism, but in this era of survival of the fittest, a nation must seek a way to survive. As we witness this stark contrast in Massawa, we think about our own situation and cannot help but feel a chill down our spines.

The mail ship left Massawa at 8 p.m., continuing towards Shanghai. Another 600 passengers boarded the ship. They were all Italian workers who had fulfilled their responsibilities to their country during the Italo-Ethiopian War. Therefore, although they were assigned to third class, they quickly occupied the decks and smoking room of the economical second class. Our athletes barely had a place to stand. Fortunately, there are not many days left in the voyage. It is estimated that we will arrive in Port Said on the 17th and disembark in Venice on the 19th.

(2)(8) Inside the Third Class

In my first letter, I mentioned the dozens of fellow countrymen in the third-class cabins. Yesterday, I visited them. In the filthy steerage and passageways, they had laid a mat on the floor for their long voyage. Compared to them, we are worlds apart.

They all wear short shirts and shorts, representing the epitome of rural life. There are a total of 130 of them, all from Zhejiang, with over 100 from Wenzhou and over 20 from Qingtian. According to them, they are all going to Europe to do business and make a living. They have not yet decided which country to go to. Some will figure it out once they get to Europe. I asked them what kind of business they would do in Europe. Apart from a few who said they brought some tea and other local products, the rest said they would see once they got to Europe. I also asked them why they insisted on going to Europe. Their answer was that they could not make a living in China. However, according to them, each person's travel expenses were at least 400 to 500 yuan. In Chinese society, with 400 to 500 yuan in capital, it is not necessarily impossible to find a way to make a living. Therefore, apart from admiring their masculinity and adventurous spirit, I am truly puzzled by their motives for going to Europe. One person told me that their tickets were purchased through an agent and cost 17 pounds. After boarding the ship, they found out that it only cost 12 pounds. The ship's meals are set at 1 pound per day for two meals, but the mail ship company only gives the cook 8 yuan. According to him, such meals from Shanghai to Venice would cost less than 2 yuan in total. Although this may be an exaggeration, it is an undeniable fact that these wandering, pitiful people are being exploited everywhere.

People from Qingtian have a long history in Europe. It is said that at the end of the Guangxu era, a person from Qingtian secretly brought some stones, a special product of Qingtian, to France and surprisingly made a fortune. After that, one person told another, and more and more people went. At its peak, there were as many as 30,000 to 40,000 people in all of Europe. There are still 30,000 people now. Some are fortunate enough to start a family and build a career abroad, but most drift in foreign lands, and their lives are still hopeless. Therefore, they will do anything. They have created many jokes abroad and left many stains on the national image. The embassies and consulates in various European countries are constantly trying to send them back to China, but the adventurous Qingtian people are still going in batches, one after another. For this newly emerging force, I can only pray that the goddess of fortune will always be with them, preserving a bit of dignity for our country. (Sent from Port Said on July 17)

Educational News

Ministry of Education Orders Issuance of Two Types of Measures for Training Teachers for Compulsory Education 210

The Ministry of Education issued an order to the education departments of various provinces and cities on the 5th, stating, "Regarding the training of teachers for the promotion of compulsory education and mass education, at the previous meeting of local senior administrative personnel, President Chiang Kai-shek suggested that improving teacher quality should be the main task for promoting compulsory education and mass education in the future. When training teachers, education departments in various provinces and cities should pay close attention to establishing temporary training classes to train unemployed graduates from secondary schools and above to serve as teachers. Furthermore, the Executive Yuan issued Instruction No. 3887 on June 25, stating that for the teachers and supervisors needed for the promotion of compulsory education and mass education in the 1936 fiscal year, most should be selected and trained from those who have graduated from junior high school, senior high school, or normal school and are currently unemployed. Education administrative agencies in various provinces and cities should select, train, and assign them. At the same time, provinces and cities should select personnel to come to Beijing for training. After the training is completed, they will return to their respective provinces and cities to handle the training of the aforementioned teachers and supervisors. Detailed plans for selection and training will be determined separately by the Ministry of Education." Upon receiving this, it is understood that the training of teachers for compulsory education and mass education and the training of personnel who organize the training of teachers for compulsory education and mass education are extremely important for the implementation of compulsory education and mass education and should be actively carried out. In addition to the measures for the training class for electro-educational personnel for mass education, which have already been promulgated, the "Measures for the Training Class for Cadre Personnel in Compulsory Education" and the "Measures for Training Classes for Compulsory Education Teachers in Various Provinces and Cities" are hereby formulated and attached to this order. Please follow the regulations of the training class measures, select qualified students, and submit the list of students to the Ministry before August 31 to participate in the training. Furthermore, please follow the regulations of the training class measures, plan and establish training classes for compulsory education teachers, and submit the plan for the number of classes to be established and the funding in advance to the Ministry for approval. The cultivation and improvement of teachers is of utmost importance, and the Ministry attaches great importance to this matter in accordance with the order. Please comply with this order."

Measures for the Training Class for Cadre Personnel in Compulsory Education

(1) The Ministry of Education is holding a training class for cadre personnel in compulsory education (hereinafter referred to as "the training class") to train cadre personnel in various provinces and cities who handle compulsory education. (2) Students of the training class will be selected by the education departments of various provinces and cities from the following personnel: 1. Administrative personnel in charge of compulsory education in various provinces and cities (director-level staff members or section chiefs of the relevant departments of various departments and bureaus). 2. Incumbent or prospective organizers of training classes for compulsory education teachers in various provinces and cities. (3) The training period for students of the training class is set at one and a half months (from September 20 to November 5, 1936). (4) The training class curriculum focuses on subjects such as spiritual lectures, administrative issues of compulsory education, textbooks and teaching methods for short-term elementary schools, and common knowledge of rural economics and public health. (5) The expenses of the training class will be paid by the Ministry of Education from the central compulsory education funds. (6) In addition to the expenses for meals, accommodation, and school supplies, which will be provided by the training class, the travel expenses of the students should be paid by the sending agency. (7) The training class will have one director and one deputy director, who will be selected and appointed by the Ministry of Education. The lecturers will be nominated by the director and submitted to the Ministry of Education for approval and appointment.

Measures for Training Classes for Compulsory Education Teachers in Various Provinces and Cities

(1) In order to train compulsory education teachers, various provinces and cities should, starting in 1936, hold training classes for compulsory education teachers under the auspices of the education departments of various provinces and cities (including the provisions of Article 15 of the Detailed Rules for the Implementation of the Outline of Temporary Measures for the Implementation of Compulsory Education). (2) The training classes for compulsory education teachers should be held centrally or in districts according to the existing normal school districts or administrative supervisory districts, depending on the circumstances of each province. Each municipality directly under the Executive Yuan should hold at least one class. (3) The expenses of the training classes for compulsory education teachers in various provinces and cities may be paid from the compulsory education funds allocated by the central government with the approval of the Ministry of Education, but may not exceed 10% of the total allocation. (4) The director of the training class for compulsory education teachers shall be appointed by various provinces and cities from among the personnel who have participated in the training class for cadre personnel in compulsory education organized by the Ministry. (5) The training class for compulsory education teachers should recruit unemployed graduates of junior high school, senior high school, normal school, or equivalent schools for selection and training. The training period is set at three to six months, respectively. (6) In addition to lecturing on laws and regulations related to compulsory education and methods and education methods for running elementary schools and short-term elementary schools, the training class for compulsory education teachers should also focus on the training of national consciousness, military training, and common knowledge of rural economics and public health. (7) Students of the training class for compulsory education teachers who have completed their studies and passed the assessment will be given a graduation certificate. (8) Graduates of the training class for compulsory education teachers should be assigned by the education departments of various provinces and cities to serve as various teachers in compulsory education or to handle local compulsory education administration as a priority. (9) When necessary, the Ministry of Education may send personnel to provide guidance to the training classes for compulsory education teachers held in various provinces and cities. (10) These measures shall be implemented from the date of promulgation.

Educational Popularization Vehicles and the Future of New Education in China (3) 212

— Written by Professor Mei Gordon, Educator at New York University, USA Translated by Liu Wufu

The economic activity report of the Nianer Cooperative in Jinjiaxiang Village illustrates the specific function of this plan. The workers in this area are mostly textile, laundry, planting, rattan craft, and hand-textile cooperative workers. Among the workers in the hand-textile cooperative, there are 20 old and two young women engaged in hand-spinning, which was forgotten by the invention of new textiles. The rattan craft cooperative is located in a member's home, where work is carried out under the management of a skilled worker. Adults only work in the evenings, while children engage in the actual work of making rattan tools during the day, or engage in reading, games, sports, storytelling, and other common gatherings. The planting cooperative manages 40 acres of farmland, with 25% of the farmland planted with wheat and the rest planted with vegetables. They have used scientific methods to improve seeds and implement crop rotation, and they have also implemented insect management. The laundry cooperative has more than 150 households, and the laundry washed is supplied by the college students participating in the cooperative. To continue to engage in this work, one must study the designated coursework.

The members of the nearby Nianer Cooperative have several fixed plans. They hold general assemblies at fixed times, renovate roadside houses, improve public health, report and discuss current events, and handle temporary medical diagnoses, etc. They have established public contracts, do not believe in religion, do not spend money on superstition, and learn to read and write five new characters every day. They get up in the morning and work and have breakfast in a very orderly manner.

It is clear that this kind of education plan is what the Chinese people need. The cultural education level of the founders of the Nianer Movement is the same as that of the intellectual class in the United States. They are leaders, they instruct the people, and they become models for modern students. They also indicate the needs of the Chinese people. We Americans have long known this from Pearl Buck's novels. The Chinese people are mostly farmers. They live in the countryside, and each person only has an income of 30 to 40 yuan per year. Their lives only rely on the simplest and most frugal standard of living. Western education not only exceeds their needs and understanding, but also exceeds their economic awareness. Due to the rapid import of Western education, the damage to society is already evident in some places. This plan is a good foundation because it plans for the development of the entire nation and is carried out gradually.

The development of the Nianer Movement is worth our attention. It is engaged in strong construction based on the good route of progressive education. Its use is based on the methods of individual needs and interests. For example, workers engaged in rattan tools can be used as the basis for mathematics education, and the quality of the harvest can be introduced into the study of the properties and effects of light. This movement is outdoor, and it stipulates that students participate in the practical work of public socio-economic life, using economic activities to connect cultural and social education. This has spread rapidly. The movement, which was established just three years ago, has spread to six provinces and established 105 cooperative organizations and other organizations, with 21,520 members. Undoubtedly, this rural education movement has been closely watched by the Central Ministry of Education. Their work on the transformation of Chinese society will arouse the interest of the whole world. (Translated from this year's June issue of "Asia" magazine)

Commercial News

After the Removal of Grain Price Limits, Flour Prices Increase Wildly by Ten Cents 213

Yesterday, the flour market presented a new situation. The exchange was ordered to remove price limits, and the January prices were opened as scheduled. However, the market had been sluggish for a month, and the rise in foreign wheat prices was drastic. Therefore, the market situation, after a sharp jump, could not avoid speculation from outside the industry. Forward prices rose by six to eight cents. Canadian prices recently rose by one yuan, and forward prices rose by eight to nine cents. Therefore, most people were unanimously enthusiastic. However, the opening price for this month was still reasonable, with an initial price of only one dime and four cents, rising to four cents and seven and a half mils, only three cents higher than the previous day. Unexpectedly, the opening price for September immediately rose by six cents, and then rose another one and a half cents. Therefore, the October price wildly increased by one dime (the exchange stipulates that the daily rise and fall cannot exceed the previous day's closing price). The November and December prices also rose by one dime each, without any other opening prices. Because there was still absorption from outside the industry, the rise moved forward without any looking back. The January price was the first time it started and had reached 3.4075 yuan. At the beginning of the second session, the price for this month wildly rose to 3.20 yuan. Later, the bulls exited, gradually falling back by two to three cents. The September price remained high, only half a cent away from the one-dime limit. The October and November prices rose to the limit, without any movement. The January price was released on a broad scale and also fell back by two to three cents. The wild and special development of the flour market cannot be predicted by common sense.

Wheat Futures Rise Sharply Following the Flour Market, Japanese Merchants Still Purchasing Spot Goods 214

Yesterday, at the opening of the wheat futures market in the morning, the prices for all months rose by five, seven, or eight cents due to the repeated rebound in foreign wheat prices. The briskness of the transactions and the frenzy of buying were rare recently. After the second session, the price for this month did not continue to surge due to large-scale continuous exits by profitable bulls due to the sharp rise in the flour market. The January price had fewer chips and also increased by seven to eight cents. In the spot wheat market, due to the continued rise in foreign wheat prices, Japanese merchants continued to purchase. The price of high-quality wheat increased by another six to seven cents, medium and secondary quality by three to five cents. Shandong Yaowan wheat opened at 4.80 yuan, Wuxi wheat at 4.71 yuan, Huaian wheat at 4.73 yuan, secondary to six cents, Puzhen wheat at 4.62-3 yuan, Suqian wheat at 4.77 yuan, Daqiao wheat at 4.65 yuan, Hankou wheat at 4.45 yuan, secondary to two cents, vehicle wheat at 4.67 yuan, secondary to five cents, Hefei wheat at 4.70 yuan, Jiangbei wheat at 4.60 yuan, and Caishi wheat at 4.64 yuan. Shenda went out for 1,000 bags. Japanese merchants purchased slightly less yesterday, only opening Hankou wheat for over 1,000 bags, with the price opening at 4.65 yuan.

New Early Rice Arrives Continuously, Ke Xian Rice Returns to a Weak State, Down One to Two Dimes Compared to the Previous Few Days 215

Yesterday, the Ke Xian rice market turned sluggish again, while the source of supply was active. New early rice also continuously arrived in Shanghai. Yesterday, another 600 bags of new Wenzhou machine rice arrived, with the price opening at 9.03 yuan. Due to the imminent influx of new rice, cargo owners and hoarders were even more eager to sell, while local buyers were not eager to buy. The market immediately weakened by a few cents to a dime or so. Compared to the highest price two or three days ago, it has decreased by a dime to two dimes. Although oil and northern gangs inquired, these two gangs only purchased 300 bags of Hunan Jinglai rice. The mainland only purchased 240 bags of Shashi rough rice and hundreds of bags of secondary Jiangxi late rice. Local demand was also weak, with total transactions of less than 3,000 bags.

Du Jian Rice Price Falls, Sales Slightly Brisk 216

(South Shanghai) Yesterday, the supply from various sources was more than before, with a total of 25 to 26 boats and over 5,000 shi of goods. Local sales were flat, and only Wei Hai Shu and other gangs purchased over 600 bags of thin paddy rice. Therefore, the market situation was difficult to turn around and remained flat and weak. In addition to the slightly supportive fresh, high-quality early japonica rice, medium and stored rice depreciated by about a dime. The thin paddy rice remained unchanged. After the price of Du Yang Jian rice fell completely, sales were slightly more brisk, so the price increased by one or two chǐ. Yinyang rice, due to shortages and brisk sales, also rose by one dime. Shenda and Dongxin machine rice arrived with a total of ten shi, and the price remained unchanged.

(North Shanghai) Yesterday, 15 to 16 boats arrived from various routes downstream. High-quality white japonica and Yang Jian rice had some transactions, medium quality rice was slightly sluggish, and thin paddy rice was scarce and still good. The remaining goods were stagnant. The market price of high-quality white refined rice was barely maintained, and medium quality rice was weak by a few cents to a dime or so. Yang Du, Bu Ke, Jian Yuan, and other types of rice were all soft, decreasing by a few cents to nearly a dime.
