Standard Yarn Cheaper Than Spot Goods: Yarn Market Showing Signs of Recovery Yesterday, Bulls Not Entirely Emerging, Market Price Rising by More Than One Yuan 218

After several days of sharp decline, the yarn market showed signs of recovery yesterday, and the situation stabilized slightly. In fact, the sharp drop of 16 or 17 yuan compared to the high price attracted profit-takers to cover their positions. At the same time, spot yarn sales were still maintained. As standard yarn prices are cheaper than spot yarn, the rebound occurred abruptly after the decline stabilized. However, bullish companies emerged one after another with huge volumes, and with new cotton soon to be on the market, there were even more who were bearish on the yarn market.

After the second session, due to the strength of raw cotton, the Three Grades of Yarn market hardened, and the market became tighter, with prices rising slowly. As a result, each month rose by seven jiao to one yuan and four jiao compared to the previous day's closing price. Short Covering: US Cotton Closing Market Rebounds 219

Yesterday, the US cotton market opened with each month rising by one to three points. Private cotton estimates varied greatly, causing buyers to wait and see, and the market was stagnant. In the early morning, the Liverpool news was good, and there was a lack of rain in Oklahoma. Traders bought in, and there were few sellers, so the market price rose. Later, because the weekly weather report was favorable, bulls closed their positions, and local traders sold, turning weak. Before the close, short positions were covered, and the market rebounded again. Spot prices fell by four points, while futures rose by six to nine points. British spot cotton fell by three points, and futures rose by three or four points. Indian cotton initially rose due to lack of rain and purchases by European exporters and speculators, but later declined due to sales by operators. The Customs gold unit was unchanged. The posted price of standard gold was reduced to 1126.9 yuan. North-South Goods: Market Situation After the Dissolution of Jin Cai Company, Traders Open Higher by About One Yuan 225

The purpose of the Jin Cai Company, since its establishment, has been to seek mutual benefit for the industry, but it has not been even a month since it was established. Now, due to differing opinions among the various firms, it has been decided to dissolve the company from yesterday, and each firm will continue to operate independently. Unexpectedly, as soon as the company was dissolved, the prices of goods from the numbered firms immediately became firmer. Yesterday, the city market opened with prices such as Da Xing Cai opening at 19.5 yuan to 18.5 yuan, up about one yuan from the previous price. The various firms all rushed to purchase, and the market势势 was greatly boosted. Subsequent defense was tight.

Piece Goods: Cotton Cloth Sales Limited to a Corner, More Additions in the Yangtze River Basin, Fewer and Fewer Routes to North China 228

Although yarn and cotton prices suddenly rebounded yesterday, due to the strong cotton production and the large amount of yarn in stock, the trend of yarn and cotton futures was weak. Although cotton cloth sales were very good, they were only limited to a corner. The Sichuan, Yangtze River, and Shaanxi routes saw slight increases, while the northern routes (Tianjin, Yantai, etc.) saw sharp decreases. The Japanese merchants' efforts to focus on North China have already been implemented, and the number of goods going to the northern route is decreasing day by day. Among the few goods going north, the woven flannel from the factories accounts for the most. Yesterday, the prices of various types of cloth were stable. Fine twill from the factories fell slightly by about 5 cents per piece. Shen Bao Literary Supplement

From Tongguan to Shouyang Mountain 244

By: Zongren

Standing by the Yellow River, on the mountain at Fengling Ferry, overlooking the opposite bank, the entire city of Tongguan seems to be displayed at the bottom of your eyes. Starting from that cluster of red houses at the Longhai Railway Station, the trees along the road stretch out like smoke and clouds, running through the ancient city, towering into distant mountains, and disappearing into a mountain cave that seems to be there and yet isn't.

Further away, thirty miles from Tongguan, is Mount Hua. The Five Elders Peaks stand verdant in the clouds and mist, and the temples on the mountainside are still faintly discernible. At the foot of Tongguan is the Yellow River, with its turbulent rapids; from time to time, the sound of splashing water and the shouts of the old boatmen on the ferry quietly rise up; in the lonely mountain bay, it seems to evoke an air of slumber.

Fengling Ferry is only thirty miles from Shouyang Mountain by mountain road. We took a ferry from Tongguan, and boarded a car that had been pre-arranged at the dock, and the journey only took forty minutes. But in these forty minutes, the encounters with reality and the nostalgic feelings, if one were a poet, would truly require dozens of poems to describe. I thought of Li Bai composing poetry in this place after getting drunk in the past, and I couldn't help but feel some silent emotion.

There is no particularly obvious distinction at this border of Shanxi and Shaanxi. If one thinks about it in detail: one can smell the scent of opium in the streets of Tongguan; one can see the dominoes game of "Ten-Nine" and fine porcelain teacups blocking the streets. But upon entering Shanxi territory, all of these change their appearance. For example, opium is renamed "medicinal cake" and issued in small quantities; gambling tools are hidden at the bottom of cabinets and sold secretly. Such is the case!

The atmosphere in both places feels the same.

This time, our trip was sponsored by the Tongpu Railway Bureau, so the car followed the base of the Tongpu Railway the whole time. And the base of the Tongpu Railway mostly relies on the Yellow River - going down, it relies on the banks of the Fen River.

According to the receptionist sent by the Railway Bureau, the entire Tongpu South Railway is scheduled to open to traffic on October 10th. Therefore, the construction is being accelerated everywhere. More and more troops transferred from various places are participating in the road construction.

The car climbed up a mountain and then drove straight down. The situation was like plunging into the vast Yellow River, which greatly increased people's sense of adventure and made us cry out in fright from time to time. Along the way, solitary stone statues standing on layers of cliffs, or even collapsed in front of ruins, greatly increased our interest.

Therefore, even though we were traveling on a hot day, we didn't feel tired at all, and time slowly slipped away in everyone's shouts of surprise and sighs of emotion! The car stopped surprisingly quickly at the foot of Shouyang Mountain.

We expected to stop at Shouyang Mountain for an hour or two. Because this place is an important station for the military to build roads, and it is also the place that our news photography team must film.

But our work did not go very smoothly. The soldiers and officers building the road all advocated caution when it came to including them in the photographs. They said that they were not prepared beforehand, so their clothes were not neat. "If it's not neat, what will it look like when it's photographed? It will damage our reputation. Let's wait until we change our clothes in the afternoon before taking pictures. Please sit down and rest first!" The deputy regiment commander in charge of road construction insisted. As a result, our work had to be delayed somewhat. But everyone was unwilling to accept their hospitality, hoping to use this free time to visit the "Two Worthies Shrine" that was so familiar in our memories.

Shouyang Mountain is not high, and the area it occupies is not large. And it looks sparse, without even a decent forest. It is somewhat bald and tailless, like a declining ruined household. But because there are historical sites to be found, everyone no longer finds its poor and sour face hateful.

Halfway up the mountain, next to the car road, there are two not very tall pagodas. A rock next to the pagodas is engraved with the words "Tomb of Bo Yi and Shu Qi" carved in the ninth year of the Republic of China. Bending around behind this pagoda, on a desolate grassy area behind the mountain, is the real Two Worthies Shrine.

Perhaps it is because people today do not respect the ancients, but the shrine has already fallen into disrepair, leaving only a few dilapidated temple buildings. And those temple buildings are now occupied by the headquarters of the [Number] Corps of the [Army]. The memorial arch in front of the shrine, like the withered cypress trees, looks very unpromising. As for the stone figures and stone horses, most of them are missing heads and legs, or even only half of them, squatting in the sand.

Next to the shrine, in a courtyard buried in weeds, are the graves of the two brothers. Bo Yi is at the top, and Shu Qi is at the bottom. Only one cypress tree in the entire shrine stands alone on Bo Yi's grave. According to legend, this is also for "righteousness." Shu Qi could not leave his elder brother, so he let a tree on his grave die and attach itself to his elder brother's grave. But it seems that the tree is very small, like a newborn, so this kind of legend about moral integrity is very questionable.

"Ignorance is great righteousness" all the inscriptions contain this meaning. I think the philosophy of Bo Yi and Shu Qi probably suited their intentions very well. Because that method of resistance of not eating Zhou millet, even to the point of starving to death, is, in the eyes of some people, the most suitable.

It was still early, so everyone left the Two Worthies Shrine and walked to the village on the mountainside. Most of the houses in this village were hidden under ancient trees. The strange thing is that there did not seem to be a single man in this village, only some women and dogs with their tails between their legs, hiding behind the women, staring at our intrusion with surprised eyes.

Because of our curiosity, we all broke into a private school. There were only some children in the private school, shaking their heads and reciting "Confucius said", and they all stopped when they saw us!

"Where is your teacher?"

"The teacher ran away!"

"He went to build the road!"

Only then did the receptionist from the Railway Bureau suddenly realize and explain to us:

"Oh, wherever the project goes, the government not only buys the people's land, but also sends the nearby residents to work. Their teacher was probably conscripted to work."

"What about the money? Is there any money? The money for the land and the wages for the work!"

"There is, but I don't know when we'll get it?"

The receptionist said meaningfully.

Melancholy 245

— By Karel Čapek (Czech)

A moment ago, you were chatting and joking, everything making you feel interested and happy. Now you are staring at the ground; you want to pray, but you don't know why or to whom. Sadness, fatigue, indifference. You find it strange that just a few minutes ago you felt happy about everything, and even stranger that you have to get up tomorrow and do your work. And worst of all, your throat feels tight, you seem to be carrying a heavy burden on your back, and your eyes are like lead, so you can't lift them from the ground.

What happened to you? Nothing, really nothing. Just one or two trivial, unpleasant things. Like something blocking my way, but it's insignificant—something unexpected, something that hurt me a little. I can't drive it from my mind. In fact, it's nothing when you put it all together; it's not even enough to be a legitimate reason for sorrow, even if you add it all up. It's nothing, but put together, it's a bit too much—actually, it's still insignificant, but you know life is a terrible thing.

I envy that day when Solomon wrote that pessimistic creed—when he wrote, "Vanity of vanities, all is vanity"—that day, nothing special had happened to him; his kingdom hadn't fallen, his beloved wife hadn't died, and he didn't feel death approaching in his ailing body. In fact, Solomon didn't encounter anything that day! But perhaps he sensed foolishness and cunning in his beloved wife's eyes, indifference in his friends, and baseness in his servants. Or maybe he lost something, something perhaps utterly insignificant; or a project of his failed, something disappointed him; he saw many events as slightly dimmer than usual, the people were baser and more annoying, and life was more difficult. All this really amounts to nothing if you put it all together. But Solomon that day was struck and trembled under the weight of these irrelevant things; tired to death, he wrote in his book, "All is vanity."

Because, you must understand, in the face of profound blows of fate, one cannot be a hero. Death, ruin, shipwrecks, some say, can be endured with a stiff upper lip; at the very end, one can still struggle before dying. But one can never be a hero in the face of a pinprick. You can actually not care about being pricked more than twice; and you can barely endure these few more times without caring; but after being pricked ten or fifteen times, all your heroism will slip away. Man is helpless against small pains. He can feel pride in losing a leg, but he feels no pride when he breaks a fingernail. He can endure the death of his wife with indifference, but he cannot heroically endure her stupid, commonplace ordinariness. He may have some consolation in the event of disaster, if his house collapses, but he has no consolation if his house is extremely simple.

Melancholy, the most serious suffering in life, is a pain caused by small reasons. It is serious because it does not yield to heroic actions; there are no heroic victims of melancholy. In any case, it is a weakness, or more precisely, a state of helplessness in the face of small misfortunes.

I would even say that there are hardly any tragedies in modern times. Take Ibsen: his modern tragedies (even including his *Ghosts*) are actually comedies of melancholy; the tragedy of the heroes in the plays is due to the fact that they are pitiful characters, inevitably heading down the path of misfortune, and because of this, they are fundamentally comical. Classical heroes rebel against the will of the gods, which is tragic; modern heroes rebel against human affairs, which is somewhat comical, but mainly miserable. Shakespeare's heroes often die, a conclusion that saves them from unwanted absurd actions. Modern heroes mostly continue to live, which makes them both comical and pitiable. If Othello hadn't killed himself, but it was discovered that he had conditions that mitigated his crime of murder, and he could even live his old age like a retired general, receiving half a pension, he would become a modern hero—that is, a melancholy, discounted hero. That is why one must create a massacre at the end of the play to write a true tragedy. It is not death itself that is tragic and sublime, but that after that, your hero can no longer do anything to undermine his heroic actions.

To be overwhelmed with suffering is a melancholy thing. If there is such a thing as modern heroism, it should not be a heroic death, but heroic optimism. But modern drama has not yet reached this level. (Translated by Luo Wei)

Yangtze River Night Tide 246

— By Chao Yi

I was silent, and he was silent too.

The night was black. I couldn't see his face or hands, but I could still see him clearly. His eyes, darker than the night, were open beside me.

Those were his eyes, indifferent and slightly melancholy when still; otherwise, they changed unfairly, flashing with pain, anger, despair, and the color of a desperate battle. In this black abyss, a world of unbreakable suffering was built; but when you yourself are in pain, you can see that its pain is sharper than yours, so sharply that you feel a little less lonely and get some warmth. But it itself is not warm; it only warms your pain with pain and saves your despair with anger. At that time, I was trapped in extreme desolation and suffering. By chance, I broke into this realm. I don't know, maybe this is what I dreamed of. Anyway, I stayed. I have been there for a long time, but I never hope to be familiar with it, and I can never recognize its true color. In it, I often feel a stinging sensation, and sometimes I smell blood and death. But I can't walk away. It's a disease, stubbornly staying in the middle of suffering, and it has become a disease that I can't cure.

I often feel that this is unreasonable. Why break in and disturb this world?

The eyes open beside me seem a little different from usual. They are still resentful, and tired, but still uneasy; this black world looks even bigger to the point of being boundless, and deeper to the point of having no bottom. Suddenly hot, suddenly frozen. Wrapping me, completely isolating me from the outside world. In the black depths, the sounds of wind and water gradually rang out, releasing the fragrance of grass and trees. I suddenly felt a sweet dizziness. I understood a little that this was just a world of illusion, which would soon disappear. But I still closed my eyes and grabbed it, begging it to let me breathe a little more of this near-death happiness.

The sounds of wind and water gradually rang out, from blurred to clear, gradually approaching from a distance. I couldn't tell whether this was an illusion or reality. So I asked him:

"What sound?"

"The tide."

It was the tide, whistling and rolling in from afar. I took off my shoes and stepped down to the ground, tiptoeing to open the window leading to the terrace. The terrace faced the滔滔(towering) river, making it easy to look at the distant water and smoke. As soon as the window opened, the wind came in first, followed by the rushing sound of water. The tide was like a white snake, dragging its tired and angry steps from afar, crashing onto the shore, and making a 呯嗙 (peng bang) desperate cry.

Under the dim light of the sky, boats with their sails full slipped across the water like dreams.

I was buried in the sounds of wind and water, buried in the沉鬱(melancholy) dimness, buried in the 呯嗙 (peng bang) desperate cry. I couldn't tell where I was and where was the world outside me.

"　　, come." A voice called to me.

It was probably the sound of the tide.

"Come!" It shouted again after a while.

Not the tide. Those black eyes were looking at me.

We all didn't speak, quietly listening to the howling of the wind and the impact of the water. I understood that the tide hated this land and wanted to wash it away and swallow it.

Gradually, the tide, the black eyes, and I all merged into one sound.

The sky was slowly lighting up.

I always hear the sounds of wind and water, but people don't allow me to speak. Okay, I won't speak: but I can still hear it.

Of the Proletariat 247

— TK

The Silent Witness 248

— By Long Gong

"He is a silent one."

Xu Jia—a very close friend of mine, said this. He left me a roll of newspapers and walked away. It was the Shen Bao. Following his instructions, I found the news in the "Local News" column: An unnamed coolie man, around forty years old, died in a cement tile pipe placed by the Public Works Department on an open space on Route Massenet in the French Concession because he had no place to live due to illness and slept there at night. He was seriously ill and died in the tile pipe, and no one noticed, causing the corpse to become fat and rotten, and the ozone was overflowing...

Such a clear description of social reality is rarely seen in newspapers. I put it down and wrapped a small book, placing it on the rattan shelf, but unintentionally found that the news was still shining brightly in front of me. I didn't fold it so it wouldn't be exposed.

It was a fat, rotten corpse steamed by the summer heat, hiding in a tile pipe and not saying a word. Around it was bright sunshine. Regarding everything about it, it refused to tell us. Had it struggled? Did it have anything to tell us when it was dying? Didn't the people related to it know about its fate?—No one can know. Tomorrow, this old newspaper will be placed in the waste paper pile, and then it will be forgotten by people, in a calmness without regret or sigh, and it will be forever disconnected from humanity. The matter is very simple.

But the non-simple place can be placed on that assumption. That assumption is that a person's birth and death, an individual's existence or disappearance, is closely related to the disasters, happiness, or progress and decline of all mankind; from the news of the death of one or several individuals, we can often observe the fate of mankind and speculate on the positive and negative mileage of its culture and the period of its collapse. If that is the case, my friend Xu Jia and I were moved for a reason.

In Shanghai, such a thing is just like seeing a dead mouse on the road. Even if you scream and avoid it, there is no emotion. I believe that is the reaction of some people. From the beginning, they treat even a living, nameless coolie the same way, either seeing him as a born slave or as a lowly compatriot.

But some people will see this corpse as a symbol of humanity's barbarism and shame, thinking it is the bone residue spat out by villains, the excrement after their brothers were swallowed by demons, and the aiming star for measuring their future destiny. Therefore, they will never forget it, mentioning it in all conversations and arguments—so that it will exist for several centuries, more long-lived than the corpses of Egyptian royalty. This is also entirely possible.

I think it is not that we abandoned him. I ask, who among us has the courage to abandon the survival of others? It was he who abandoned us. He had a stronger body and more courage than us. Doing more work, yet he abandoned us.

This is our shame. It proves our selfishness, hesitation, and inability to cooperate with him. It even proves that we are existences that are inferior to him and more in need of appeasement.

"The silent witness is the most powerful." I remembered this sentence.

Night Watch 249

— By Huo Bao

It's my turn to stand watch on the night shift line,

I stand in the middle of the graveyard, looking around;

There are countless sentinels,

Who have died for us;

Countless lives have died in the ancient无间(Avici hell),

Also to fight for the prosperity of the next generation.

To fight for the light of the new era,

Forget all the current terror and cold.

When the light comes,

They are already lying in the loess, sleeping peacefully.

Time has arranged this fate

Now it's my turn to tread this death line.

Where to find a way out in the graveyard of the black night?

Wholeheartedly waiting for the dawn of tomorrow.

Only asking before dying,

To be worthy of oneself, worthy of humanity,

—苟延性命(prolonging life), dying with regret,

That is the most terrible sorrow!

Brothers, when the sun rises,

Or maybe I am already tired,

At that time, I will hand over the shift to you.

History has passed down a stern command:

To guard the front to the death!

The Strong Character of the Nation 250

— By Qu Yi

Gorky, in his essay "On Drama," said this:

"The basic mission of art must transcend reality, and look at today's cause from the height of the glorious goal built by the creators of the new mankind—the working class... Heroic deeds must have heroic language."

In another place, he said:

"The modern heroes—scholars, inventors, builders, Komsomol Ploneers, poets—have not yet been noticed, and even if they are noticed, they are still decorated with soulless language."

Gorky often called on young Soviet writers to write a typical new hero who creates a second nature.

In the current stage of China, what kind of typical new hero do we require of literature? Our heroes must possess a huge national soul and be able to make strong and unyielding resistance to all oppressors.—Our heroes must be the strong character of the nation.

Recently, after reading several novels by Shu Qun, I saw the expression of such a strong character. The first article published in "Literature" *The Child Without a Homeland*, Guoli and Guolisha have the same aspect of a strong character, one showing the perseverance of not having a homeland, and the other showing contempt for people who live like mice. However, Guoli finally put a knife into the devil's chest. He was checked on the road, but he was willing to admit that he was Korean and be bound, dedicating the magnificent soul of the nation. Next, he published "Sparks in the Desert" in the literary world. Like the previous article, he also wrote a tough and persevering Sadartu and a rough and tough A Huta. Under their various misunderstandings and tolerances, sparks finally broke out when they went on an expedition against the Mongolian bandits. And in "Mongolian Night" (see "Guangming" Issue 1), he wrote about the strength of a young man resisting the war and the calm and adaptability of a woman. Until her death, the woman also snatched the enemy's bayonet, showing an unyielding spirit of resistance. From Guoli to Sadartu and even this Mongolian woman, the author has given them all a persevering, calm, but extremely brave soul. Although A Huta was a little irritable, in his honesty and bravery, he also possessed the precious and strong character of the Chinese masses.

Then the author expanded this strong character to another side. In "Xiao Ling" in the second issue of "Literature," the author wrote about a lively female student's resistance to feudal forces with a very lively tone. The ensuing "Incident" made her an active anti-imperialist element. However, Zhang Xun, a mild-mannered instructor with feudal ideas, fulfilled his dog's role in the incident. In this combination, the contrast between the characters of the two nations is very meaningful. In "Dead and Undead" in the July issue of "Literature," the author also wrote about Li Jin, who has the same strong character as Xiao Ling, and Li Jin's woman, who has the same stubbornness as the Mongolian woman.—This woman, when her husband was tied out to be "executed with," stabbed herself in the chest and died. Although she could not get rid of the shackles of old ideas; continuing her husband's cause with her life; but with her magnificent behavior, compared with those traitors who sell the life of the nation like prostitutes, she is still worthy of admiration.

In short, all the characters written by Shu Qun are very strong in character, and this very strong character is revealed under the entire crisis of the nation. However, they are all unified and revealed under the spirit of anti-imperialism. We don't know if this is what the author intended to write. However, this is the author's personal participation in the anti-Japanese war in the Northeast Anti-Japanese Volunteer Army, which we can imagine. We believe that at this time in China, the creation of a strong national character in literature will be more important than anything else. National defense literature will have its brilliant foundation on this point.

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Talks

Talking About Pedicures 251

— By Me

As the saying goes, "Haircuts and baths are slightly interesting." In fact, haircuts and baths are not very interesting. What is interesting is pedicures, because of physiological needs and the progress of the times. After pedicures, there are foot scrapings, and after foot scrapings, there are foot massages. New patterns emerge and skills abound. If we invite textual researchers to examine the history of pedicures meticulously and one by one, wouldn't it be possible to create a great work?

According to a recent report in a certain newspaper, Mr. Xu Shiying, our ambassador to Japan, had a habit of getting pedicures when he was in the country. After going to Japan, his feet and toes suddenly became very itchy, which he couldn't solve, causing him to be restless day and night. Coincidentally, he met a certain gentleman from Shanghai who was familiar with the situation in Japan, so he asked him to find a pedicurist. The gentleman found a Japanese barber, but his skills were not very good, causing Ambassador Xu's toes to bleed and be broken, and he was extremely frustrated.

Pedicures are originally a small art, and it is not an easy task. Even in our country, which is famous for its good pedicures, it is not easy to find truly skilled pedicurists, and barbers are specialized in doing upper-class work, while pedicurists are specialized in doing lower-class work. Their habits have their own specializations, and their positions are not equal. Now, Ambassador Xu wants to张冠李戴 (put a hat on someone else's head), using a barber to do pedicuring work. It's really like "asking a cooper to build a house." It is appropriate that he should sacrifice his blood and make a big sale.

Moreover, from the great principle of human equality, it seems too far against humanitarianism for one person to be sleeping leisurely on a tatami and another person to be sitting next to him giving a pedicure. In fact, there are many examples of violating humanitarianism in the world, not just pedicures. Therefore, the current government has issued a clear order prohibiting this kind of inhumane behavior in bathrooms, which is originally correct. According to this statement, Ambassador Xu is inevitably suspected of violating the order, but from the principle of making money, this is indeed a way to make money. Assuming that you want customers' legal tender to willingly take it out of their pockets, in addition to剥猪罗玀 (skinning pigs), there is no way to achieve the goal without using this method. Therefore, assuming that you want to eliminate this lower-level work, to be honest, it is cutting off their livelihood.

Therefore, I realize that there are only two ways to make money, hard work and soft deception. Haircuts use knives, and pedicures also use knives, and these knives are better the sharper they are, clearly indicating a threatening method. On the one hand, they use their hands to massage you, massaging you until your bones are tired and you can't resist. This is a soft deception method. Threat and soft deception are used together, and the customer's money will naturally be willingly and quickly taken out of their wallet.

Now Japan's approach to China also mostly uses pedicuring methods. What they call "diplomatic unification" is to use both hard and soft methods. First the three northeastern provinces, then the four northeastern provinces, and then the eastern Hebei and northern Chahar. Now they are taking it a step further to completely control North China. This kind of pedicuring political wrist is coming in step by step, making people feel at ease and frustrated. How can this be done?

Rain 252

— Harris

The rain is drizzling again.

If I had known that this summer would be so rainy, I should have saved a few dollars to buy a new raincoat. That day, Chu Zi came from the south, and I made a special trip to Taikoo Wharf to meet him, only to encounter rain halfway. Raindrops the size of beans hit the glass of the tram window, then flowed down, winding and blurring everything on the street. There were only a few people sparsely in the carriage. It was dusk, and after the ticket seller turned on the electric lights in the carriage, he stood blankly to the side, humming a Peking opera tune. When we arrived at the Bund, the rain was even heavier, pattering on the asphalt road. I had no rain gear at all. I hesitated on the platform, and since the tram was about to leave, I had to jump off and run towards the wharf.

I waited at the wharf for about twenty minutes, taking in the rainy scenery of the Huangpu River. There was no feeling of affection, only an unusual sense of depression and annoyance. I was wondering: what will Chu Zi bring me? He came from my hometown, and I have been wandering abroad for eight whole years.

Chu Zi's face showed a smile warmed by friendship; but covered in travel dust, having crossed the southern sea, he ultimately showed signs of fatigue and was eager to find lodging. Seeing that I was almost completely drenched by the rain, Chu Zi must have felt my enthusiasm in welcoming him in the rain, holding my hand and thanking me repeatedly. I quickly said to him:

"Why are you suddenly being so polite? Is it because we've been separated for three years? ...When I came out just now, the sky was only overcast, and it only started raining halfway."

So, on the carriage to the hostel, amidst the pattering rain, Chu Zi brought news of the abundant rain in our hometown. "It's really been raining a lot in our hometown this year," he began, "In the spring," there were seven consecutive days of rain. The rice seedlings planted in the fields were all ruined by the flood, and the field ridges were submerged, with no clear boundary. The water in the ponds overflowed, and Third Uncle, who raises fish, was so flustered that he didn't even have time to eat. Flooding! Ah, can you imagine our hometown after the flood!"

Our hometown is desolate and broken! That's what Chu Zi brought. At night, I came back and lay alone in bed, turned off the lights, and the sound of raindrops outside was even clearer. A whole series of memories surfaced, back when Chu Zi and I were both still children. In spring, peach blossoms bloomed fragrantly in the fields, dotting the green lawns. Orioles sang, their chirping voices waking me up from my dreams early in the morning. The fields were green, the sky was bright, swallows murmured under the eaves, and the front of the house was bathed in warm sunlight. Every day, I lived in the southern countryside with a carefree heart. Not understanding the ways of the world, I hid under the eaves to watch the lotus leaves in the pond, spread out like fans, holding crystal-like water droplets. In summer, lotus flowers bloomed, attracting buzzing bees, and also enlivening the hearts of us children. That time was so warm and beautiful, so unforgettable...

The longing for my hometown tormented me; the pattering night rain tormented me.

Wandering in the metropolis, walking alone on the journey of life, I lack so much the warmth of sunshine, and I am always stumbling in the mud of rainy days. Chu Zi understands me and sympathizes with me. He has comforted me and encouraged me with a grateful warmth.

And it's raining again, such a sad, gray rainy day!

Rickshaw Puller 253

— Fei Xiangdong

When our family's rickshaw puller left, he introduced Ya Xiang and said, "I'm afraid I can't pull the rickshaw anymore because I'm getting old, so I resigned to your master. Now, I'm calling Ah Xiang to pull the master's rickshaw; look at this guy; he's young and strong, the master will definitely like him!"

The one being called "master" was my father. At this time, Ah Xiang was dressed in very tattered clothes, and his appearance was very unsightly. If you looked at him closely, you could see that his face still had not-so-obvious pockmarks. His body was very strong, his height was quite tall, and his strength was no problem. My father asked him a few simple questions, such as whether he was familiar with the streets of Shanghai, and then accepted him, and immediately gave him two dollars, telling him to make two sets of clothes. This made him grateful and thanking him repeatedly, and he left.

The next day, he began to pull my father to his office, and then pulled him back for lunch. We treated him very well, letting him live in the attic room. My father was not good at socializing; except for the four trips in and out a day, he rarely went anywhere else. I didn't take the rickshaw, but I sometimes had the opportunity to get close to Ah Xiang. That was when we were both staying at home at night, people were putting their minds into mahjong or chatting, but I liked to stand by the door, quietly thinking about things, looking at the stars in the sky. Ah Xiang often tidied up the rickshaw there, sometimes even washing the dirty wheels with water. When he found me standing next to him, he politely called me "young master" and asked me why I hadn't gone back to my room to rest. At first, I only talked to him about how hot the weather was, or how the rickshaw puller's life was; although it was also very hard work, compared to the rickshaw pullers who were like cattle and horses, he couldn't help but say, "I am much happier."

As we became more and more familiar, we talked more. I knew Ah Xiang. Originally had a very decent family and a wife. They diligently cultivated the land for the landlord, and they could still make a living for the family. However, in recent years, natural and man-made disasters have come together, and the landlord's rent cannot be escaped, so they had to borrow money. So, in addition to the various exploitations that farmers cannot escape, Ah Xiang also owed debts, eroded by interest, and became more and more embarrassed day by day, almost unable to live. Later, he put the burden of the family on his brother's shoulders and wandered alone to the city. Most of his current monthly income has to be sent home.

"Young master, you people who are used to enjoying blessings, how can you imagine the suffering of our villagers?" He shook his head and sighed, ending his speech.

Every time a letter came from home, he would hold it to show me, asking me to explain the meaning of the letter to him. Because of my question, "Do you want to write a reply?" he indicated that he wouldn't dare to trouble me to do such a thing. However, I took him to my father's study, opened the letter paper, and told him to say what he wanted to say.

"Young master, tell her: I am very safe here. I send money home every time I get it. ...Ask her if the child has grown up a bit? Take good care of them. Also, the debt at Uncle Li Ba's place, I will definitely be responsible for paying it off, tell my brother to rest assured. ...That's it, there's nothing else to say."

"Really nothing else to say?"

"Yes. Our villagers' words count as one word!"

Ah Xiang's honesty and kindness were obviously liked by my father as well. However, there was always some kind of barrier between us. Every time I heard his trembling voice calling me "young master," I felt uneasy. Moreover, Ah Xiang slowly realized after mixing in the city for a long time how different this cattle-and-horse life was from our comfort. Once I heard him say such words to others: "We are also people, why can others sit in a rickshaw, but I must pull the rickshaw?" Turning around to see me walking past, he stopped immediately. I didn't blame him, I simply had nothing else to say: I walked into the door, and Ah Xiang must have watched me go, right.

Two years passed like this, and Ah Xiang also resigned from my home. He wasn't doing it because he was old, but because he was going to work in a factory. He didn't introduce a new rickshaw puller to us, and my father didn't take the rickshaw anymore.

The Farmer Who Grows Watermelons 254

— Ying Dai

Growing watermelons is also a sideline in the countryside, and in some places, the farmers are unwilling to grow rice and only grow watermelons, because if the year is good and the watermelons sell for a good price, the profit is far greater than growing rice and wheat; for this reason, many farmers rely on growing watermelons to make a living.

However, the fertilizer used to grow watermelons is more than that used for rice and wheat, and if the harvest is bad and the watermelons don't sell for a good price, the loss is more severe than growing other things; therefore, prudent farmers will never grow too many watermelons, and even if they do, it will only be a few acres, as an accessory.

Watermelons are sown after Qingming. The ridges must be picked high, and ditches must be made on both sides, so that rainwater can be discharged very smoothly. It is said that dry soil is good for growing watermelons, and some people even say that a piece of land that has grown watermelons this year cannot be grown again next year, at least not for

Page 20

ten years. If the same field is grown this year and then again next year, the watermelon will be bland and tasteless. However, ordinary farmers, if he grows ten acres of watermelons, and if he wants to grow ten acres every year, and the field that has been grown is separated by ten years before growing watermelons again, then he must have one hundred acres of land to be able to rotate, but in fact, where would he have one hundred acres of land? Therefore, it will never be separated by ten years before planting again. At most, it is separated by three to five years. However, it is very good to grow watermelons in this field this year and rice next year, so experienced farmers alternate between watermelons and rice.

After planting watermelons, the most important part of the work is to press the vines, because when the watermelon vines grow long, they must be pressed down with mud in a straight line, otherwise the vines of this one and that one will cross and the watermelons will be bad or mutated. During the plum rain season, the weather can determine the fate of watermelon growers, because every day of rain or flooding will cause the watermelon vines to rot and the watermelon fruit to be not sweet. The method of growing watermelons also varies. Shandong people are famous for growing watermelons. They only leave one watermelon on each plant and pick the rest off. As for the farmers near Shanghai, they leave two or three on each plant, the so-called first vine watermelon, second vine watermelon, and last vine watermelon, so the watermelons grown by Shandong people are huge, with the heaviest weighing thirty or forty catties!

After the farmer grows the watermelons and brings them to the market for sale, in our countryside, he cannot sell them directly to the consumers, but must go through the hands of the local goods store. However, the local goods store takes a profit of one-tenth in the process, so the farmer only gets nine dollars for every ten dollars of watermelons sold, and the local goods store owner makes a profit without labor, only making the watermelon-growing farmers suffer more exploitation.

In Shanghai, aren't there local goods stores in Shiliupu, Xinzha Bridge, and Laozha Bridge? Therefore, people who grow watermelons also have to go to the local goods store when they transport watermelons to Shanghai, and then the local goods store sells them to wholesalers, retailers, or consumers. Of course, the local goods store can also get a profit of one-tenth in the middle, and the watermelon dealers have to make money through several turnovers. The farmer's multiple layers of exploitation are quite pitiful to say. In addition, in recent years, ice cream and soda have flooded the market in Shanghai, and the selling price of watermelons will not be high, only making the watermelon-growing farmers work hard for three months, and the result is that it is difficult to make a profit.

The Incense Thief 255

— Qi Ying

—One of the Mountain Travel Notes

In the summer of 1935, a few young companions and I mustered up our courage and traveled to the remote mountains and wilderness of northern Jiangxi. After crossing the Lion Ridge of Dalong Mountain, my companions and I all felt very tired, because everyone was carrying nearly 20 catties of dry food bags, and had already walked more than 20 li for half a day. A double-barreled shotgun weighing more than ten catties was also constantly moved to everyone's shoulders in turn. It was our weapon to defend against wild beasts and local bandits in this sparsely populated mountain.

There are no large trees with dense shade on Lion Ridge. The red sun spits out fierce flames, covering the entire mountain ridge. There is no path, and sharp stones and wild grass grow in disorder, making people afraid to move forward, as if venomous fire-tongue snakes are winding all over the place. Two of our friends frowned and began to complain; "If we had known that there were no trees on the mountain ridge to hide from the shade, we shouldn't have rested in the valley for a while longer, and we shouldn't have walked so fast!"

We had no choice but to straighten our backs and move forward, shifting the dry food bag on our shoulders. Lifting our heads, the mountain peak towering into the clouds opposite was placed before our eyes again. It was filled with white mist and emitting hot green smoke, and yellow sand seemed to be flying in the air. Everyone couldn't help but shudder, and a burst of hot sweat poured out of their pores.

In this Dalong Mountain, which winds for hundreds of miles, there are no houses. We had to rush to Xingzi County before the sun set to find a place to stay. Lion Ridge is about 30 li away from Xingzi County, although the sun tells us it is still early.

After descending Lion Ridge, it is a dark and deep valley, and a cool breath drilled into our hearts and lungs, and everyone couldn't help but have their souls flying. We sat down by the stream, the spring water flowed slowly, making a "嚓嚓" sound. The stream was uneven, and the spring water rushed up violently, and then suddenly flowed down, the sound of knocking on the bluestone slab seemed to be playing pleasant music for us.

Everyone took out the bread from their dry food bags to fill their stomachs, and poured the spring water into their mouths with their hands. The water was as clear and cool as ice. We ate and drank, simply forgetting to hurry on our way.

At some point, two people came down from the mountain peak on our way. It was not until these two people approached us that they were discovered by our young companion, Xiao Wang. They were all wearing a set of black cloth short jackets and trousers, and they were carrying a heavy bamboo basket in their hands. One of them asked us in a rough voice; "Hey, folks, (note) is this the way to Nanchang Prefecture?" He pointed to a small road on the side of the valley in front.

After we told him, they strode away. Our young companion Xiao Wang said in surprise; "Alas, I was scared to death! These two guys must not be good people, look, how terrible those fierce, pointed eyes are!"

However, none of us felt that way, and without caring, everyone stood up, put the food bag back on their shoulders, and we were also preparing to hurry on our way. At this time, the sun had already slanted a little to the west.

Along the way, our young companion Xiao Wang kept chattering that those two guys were not good people.

Just stepping on the high peak, more than a dozen people suddenly ran in front of us, some holding shoulder poles in their hands, and some holding spears. As soon as they ran to our front, they asked in panic; "Gentlemen, did you see two people carrying bamboo baskets in their hands?"

Movie

"Guangling Tide" Rushes to Produce Costumes 260

This is an unprecedented record in the film industry. The Yi Hua Film Company, due to the filming of "Guangling Tide," has specially set up a garment workshop within the company, inviting more than 30 tailors from outside to work day and night to rush-produce the costumes for "Guangling Tide."

We know that "Guangling Tide" is a depiction of the corruption of officials in the late Qing Dynasty, as well as the fearless struggle of revolutionary pioneers who spare no effort and regard death as home in order to fight for national liberation. The story is tragic and passionate, and the plot is shocking and moving.

Because its background is in the Qing Dynasty, the costumes and other items must be suitable for the era. Therefore, Yi Hua's costume room is like an ancient costume exhibition, with all kinds of costumes, which seem quite novel from today's perspective. Various costumes are being completed one after another by the hands of more than 30 tailors, and then hung in the wardrobe. This kind of practice of asking tailors to the company to make costumes is indeed an unprecedented initiative. The money spent on costumes for "Guangling Tide" is at least three thousand gold pieces.

Li Silian and Howard's Silhouette 261

— Lai

An artist with a solitary personality

Among the many busy people in Hollywood, he is one of them. In addition to running back and forth between Hollywood, New York, and London, busy filming and acting, he also writes screenplays. "Murry Hill" was a sensational screenplay written and performed by him. In addition, he also frequently contributes to many publications, magazines, and monthly publications such as Vanity Fair and New York, mostly discussing theories or dramas. He hopes to become a film director, and he collects all materials related to film.

Thus, his free time is very little. Sometimes he is seen playing with his two children, whom he loves more than his wife. He loves taking pictures. Whenever he is free, he always has a camera in his hand.

He plays tennis very well, and he is also a strong swimmer. However, he likes polo the most. He raises four or five trained horses himself, and his heroic figure is often seen on the wilderness field. He also likes raising dogs, and has many, but they don't have any real use.

Living a very simple life, he and his wife and two children live in a just barely adequate house. He doesn't care about clothes at all. He usually loves to wear an old-fashioned pair of flannel pants, a short plaid top, and a floral scarf, looking very unlike a "sharp-headed guy." He loves to dance, but he dances badly. He also likes to sing, but he always sings in the bathroom, never opening his mouth in front of people. He loves to eat beef steak, the fattier the better, but he is as thin as a monkey, with a long face. He likes to take walks, and is often seen wandering alone in the woods for the whole afternoon. He has light reddish-brown hair, is five feet ten inches tall, and weighs one hundred and forty-five pounds.

"The Martyrdom of a Famous Scholar" is a play he co-starred with Bette Davis, the影后 of 1935. He also performed this play on stage. His new film is Shakespeare's masterpiece "Romeo and Juliet," starring Norma Shearer, produced by MGM. It is currently being actively filmed and will soon be completed. (Guang)

Random Notes 262

Five Star Film Company hosted the press and "screenwriters" at the Dengtuomo Hotel. Zhou Jianyun gave a long speech at the banquet, which has been recorded in the newspaper, so it is omitted here. However, the final "entertainment" can still be recorded for everyone's amusement. He talked about Gao Zhanfei leaving Star, and some people think it is Star's "violent storm." What is this saying? Regarding the love dispute between Pan Zinong and Shu Xiuwen, Zhou always stood in the position of reconciliation. The newspaper reported something about Yao Xinnong, and Zhou Jianyun said that I am not their parent. What is this saying? Although the "entertainment" made some people "unhappy again," the laughter was very high at the time.

Regarding the filming of "The Bewildered Lamb," Ge Zuo Zhi, who had been growing his hair for nearly a year, has completely shaved his head, like a little monk.

The Star Film Company's music department has hired four professors to train singing and music theory. Training has already begun in recent days. In addition to four hours of basic music theory together each week, there is also individual training for actors. Star employees also have a choir.

The young Ye Fenjun has recently formed a "Drama Movement Society" and will soon perform the play "Who is a Traitor." He has also formed a singing group to broadcast patriotic songs, and has been contacting various radio stations in recent days.

In Jin Yan's "Waves Washing Sand," he played A Long, drifting to a deserted island, and eventually his white bones were abandoned on the ground. Now in "Go to Nature," he plays Ma Long, also doing the same thing, drifting to a deserted island. But in this film, he survives from a dead end and becomes a hero of the times.
